Figure 17. Typical examples of cathode materials for SIBs. (a) Schematic illustration, (b) charge/discharge curves at  $0.1\mathrm{C}$ , and (c) cycling performance at  $1\mathrm{C}$  of the  $\mathrm{Na}_{7/9}\mathrm{Cu}_{2/9}\mathrm{Fe}_{1/9}\mathrm{Mn}_{2/3}\mathrm{O}_2$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 159. Copyright 2015 Wiley-VCH. (d) Schematic illustration, (e) typical charge/discharge curves at  $0.1\mathrm{C}$  in the voltage range of 1.5 and  $3.9\mathrm{V}$ , and (f) long-term cycling performance of  $\mathrm{Na}_{0.66}\mathrm{Mn}_{0.66}\mathrm{Ti}_{0.34}\mathrm{O}_2$  at  $0.1\mathrm{C}$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 160. Copyright 2015 Wiley-VCH. (g) Schematic crystal structure of  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{VTi}(\mathrm{PO}_4)_3$ . (h) Galvanostatic charge/discharge profiles for the 1st, 2nd, 3rd, 5th, 10th, and 30th cycles between 1.5 and  $4.5\mathrm{V}$  at a current density of  $0.1\mathrm{C}$  of  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{VTi}(\mathrm{PO}_4)_3@C$  electrode. (i) Long-term cycling performance at a current rate of  $10\mathrm{C}$  of the symmetric full cells based on  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{VTi}(\mathrm{PO}_4)_3@C$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 165. Copyright 2017 Springer Nature.

![](images/7b1fc26b2296265e0eab04d23823a3543e8882e95762f37c819e4747e5537696.jpg)

![](images/f4ada75d8a8269f6b7fec9aa9b871a02ae366e72f4b4fc74fc874a8aa8f679d7.jpg)

elements, is their poor electrical conductivities, which seriously restrict their rate capability and loading of active mass. $^{135,149}$

To date, many researchers have tried to solve these challenges of alloy-based anode materials for SIBs. For instance, Cui and co-workers reported a hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers to provide an elastic buffer layer to accommodate the anisotropic volumetric expansion during the sodiation process.[150] Figure 16d shows the structural evolution of the sandwiched phosphorene-graphene structure during sodiation. The cycling performance of the phosphorene-graphene hybrids with various carbon/phosphorus (C/P) mole ratios is shown in Figure 16e. The galvanostatic cycling at  $0.02\mathrm{C}$  revealed that the samples prepared using C/P ratios of 2.78:1 and 3.46:1 exhibited similar capacity retention after 100 cycles. A lower

C/P ratio was obviously beneficial to specific capacity, given that graphene is electrochemically inactive for sodiation. To alleviate the volume expansion problem in  $\mathrm{SnO}_2$ , Zhang and co-workers evaluated a new amorphous carbon-coated  $\mathrm{SnO}_2$  electrodeposited porous CNF (PCNF@SnO₂@C) composite that not only had high sodium storage capability but also maintained its structural integrity during ongoing repetitive cycles.[152] During electrochemical operation, the CE for the PCNF@  $\mathrm{SnO}_2@\mathrm{C}$  composite anode increased to  $94.1\%$ . This composite anode also demonstrated high capacity of  $374\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$ , capacity retention of  $82.7\%$ , and high CE of  $98.9\%$  after the 100th cycle. Similarly, the same group of researchers have reported a reduced graphene oxide (RGO) incorporated SnSb@CNF (SnSb@RGO@CNF) composite anode for SIBs, achieving high capacity of  $490\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  at the 10th cycle with high capacity retention of

$87.2\%$  and a high CE of  $97.9\%$  at the 200th cycle. $^{153}$  In addition, it is vital to consider the innately poor conductivity and slow kinetics of the electrode materials. Wang and co-workers studied the electrochemical performance of  $\mathrm{SnP}_3 / \mathrm{C}$  anodes prepared by reactive ball milling of Sn, red phosphorus, and carbon black (CB) mixtures (Figure 16f). This  $\mathrm{SnP}_3 / \mathrm{C}$  anode can reversibly react with Na through conversion and alloy reaction processes. $^{151}$  It also provided high capacity of  $810\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  at  $150\mathrm{mA g}^{-1}$  for 150 cycles, thereby outperforming P, Sn, and Sn-P compound anodes for Na-ion batteries (Figure 16g). Later, Wen and co-workers prepared 3D hierarchical nanohybrids with tin sulfide nanoparticles decorating nitrogen-doped carbon nanosheet networks as an anode material for SIBs. $^{154}$  Upon cycling, the anode exhibited outstanding electrochemical performance in terms of high capacity ( $902\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  at the current rate of  $0.1\mathrm{C}$ ) and long-term stable cycling performance even after 1000 charge and discharge cycles. Last but not least, the organic compound materials also constituted a category of SIB anode materials due to their low cost and environmental friendliness. $^{155}$  Therefore, high capacity and stable anode materials for SIBs need further exploration.

3.4.2. Cathode Materials for SIBs. High-performance cathode materials for SIBs mainly consist of  $\mathrm{NaMO}_2$  (solid solutions of  $\mathrm{NaCoO}_2$ ,  $\mathrm{NaNiO}_2$ ,  $\mathrm{NaMnO}_2$ , and  $\mathrm{NaFeO}_2$ ), openframework polyanionic, Prussian blue analogue (PBA), and organic compounds. $^{156,157}$  These materials have been sought for many years owing to their high energy densities and good stability. $^{149}$  In particular, layered  $\mathrm{NaMO}_2$  have attracted great interest as cathode materials for SIBs because of their high theoretical capacity (e.g.,  $243.8\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  for  $\mathrm{O3 - NaMnO_2}$ ) and relatively simple synthesis process. $^{156}$  The electrochemical activity of layered  $\mathrm{NaMO}_2$  as a cathode for SIBs was originally reported around 1980. $^{136}$  Recent reports have highlighted manganese and iron oxides, and their combinations with a ternary element, which have been the most viable selections for cathodes. Layered oxides can mainly be classified into P2 and O3 according to the oxygen stacking sequence and coordination environment of the alkali ions. $^{158}$  The “P” and “O” represent the prismatic and octahedral sites being occupied by  $\mathrm{Na^{+}}$ . In addition, the “2” and “3” indicate the number of oxygen stacking layers in a unit cell. The O3-type compounds have higher reversible capacity, but their cycling stability is not up to the mark. $^{136}$  In contrast, the P2-type compounds deliver good cycling performance and rate capability because they provide larger active sites for the transport of  $\mathrm{Na^{+}}$ . $^{136}$  For instance, Hu and co-workers have synthesized a novel air-stable P2- $\mathrm{Na}_{7 / 9}\mathrm{Cu}_{2 / 9}\mathrm{Fe}_{1 / 9}\mathrm{Mn}_{2 / 3}\mathrm{O}_2$  cathode material for SIBs. $^{159}$  As shown in Figure 17a,  $\mathrm{Na}_{7 / 9}\mathrm{Cu}_{2 / 9}\mathrm{Fe}_{1 / 9}\mathrm{Mn}_{2 / 3}\mathrm{O}_2$  exhibits a P2-type structure, which can play a role in minimizing electrostatic repulsion between sodium ions. The initial discharge capacity is  $89\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$ , corresponding to  $0.356\mathrm{e}^{-}$  transfer, as shown in Figure 17b. The profile can be divided into two sloping regions, indicating a solid solution reaction instead of phase transition and disordered arrangement of Cu, Fe, and Mn. Upon cycling, this cathode material showed long cycling stability as demonstrated by the capacity retention of  $85\%$  after 150 cycles at  $1^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$  (Figure 17c). Hu and co-workers have also designed a novel sodium-rich tunnel-type cathode material with a nominal composition of  $\mathrm{Na_{0.66}Mn_{0.66}Ti_{0.34}O_2}$  to enhance the achievable capacity of  $\mathrm{Na_{0.44}MnO_2}$ , as shown by the schematic in Figure 17d. $^{160}$  Further, in Figure 17e, the  $\mathrm{Na_{0.66}Mn_{0.66}Ti_{0.34}O_2}$  cathode exhibits a sloping voltage profile different than the traditional  $\mathrm{Na_{0.44}MnO_2}$  electrode. This cathode material delivers high

reversible capacity of about  $74\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  and well-retained capacity after 400 cycles at a current density of  $0.1\mathrm{C}$  (Figure 17f). Due to the inexpensive constituent metal elements, the development of layered cathode materials is expected to get much attention.

Much research effort has recently been focused on polyanionic compound-based cathode materials for SIBs because of their structural diversity and stability. Although the presence of heavy polyanion groups generally reduces the gravimetric capacity of electrode materials, some of the various polyanion species (e.g.,  $\mathrm{PO}_4^{3-}$ ,  $\mathrm{SO}_4^{2-}$ ,  $\mathrm{SiO}_4^{4-}$ , and  $\mathrm{P}_2\mathrm{O}_7^{4-}$ ) in nature offer great opportunities to identify new open framework crystal structures with promising electrochemical properties.[140] In addition, the strong covalent bonding of  $\mathrm{X}-\mathrm{O}$  ( $\mathrm{X}=\mathrm{P}$ , S, Si, and B) in the crystal structure provides robust redox kinetics during electrochemical cycling, and the inductive effect of polyanion groups ensures a high operating potential, which further increases the energy density of SIBs.[140,157]  $\mathrm{Na}_3\mathrm{V}_2(\mathrm{PO}_4)_3$  as a Na super ionic conductor (NASICON) compound has been intensively investigated as a promising cathode for SIBs due to its open framework crystal structure enabled fast  $\mathrm{Na}^+$  ion conduction.[140] More recently, various V-based intercalation compounds have also been reported as high-energy cathodes based on the multielectron redox reactions of  $\mathrm{V}^{2+}/\mathrm{V}^{3+}$ ,  $\mathrm{V}^{3+}/\mathrm{V}^{4+}$ , and  $\mathrm{V}^{4+}/\mathrm{V}^{5+}$ .[139] Much effort has been focused on improving the electrochemical properties of the  $\mathrm{Na}_3\mathrm{V}_2(\mathrm{PO}_4)_3$  electrode by carbon coating and nanoscale constructing.[161-163]

Some research has mainly focused on the symmetric cells based on the same intercalation-type compound due to the various valence states of the V element. $^{164-166}$  In addition, suitable voltage of these symmetric cells can solve the safety concern of sodium dendrites at low working potentials along with reducing manufacturing costs in the fabrication processes. $^{140}$  However, it should be noted that the high rate capability and lifespan of the symmetric cell can be further improved to enhance their usability for large-scale applications. However, challenges remain in the development of suitable electrode materials to enable long lifespan and high-rate capability. In this regard, Du and co-workers have prepared a sodium superionic conductor structured electrode, sodium vanadium titanium phosphate  $\left(\mathrm{Na}_{2} \mathrm{VTi}(\mathrm{PO}_{4})_{3}\right)$ , by a sol-gel method. $^{165}$  The corresponding schematic is shown in Figure 17g, which illustrates the structure of  $\mathrm{Na}_{2} \mathrm{VTi}(\mathrm{PO}_{4})_{3}$ , consisting of corner-sharing  $\left[\mathrm{TiO}_{6}\right] / \left[\mathrm{VO}_{6}\right]$  octahedra and  $\left[\mathrm{PO}_{4}\right]$  tetrahedral sites. Further, Figure 17h shows that the three plateaus of 3.4, 2.1, and  $1.6 \mathrm{~V}$  in the discharge profile correspond to the conversion reaction of  $\mathrm{V}^{4+} \rightarrow \mathrm{V}^{3+}$ ,  $\mathrm{Ti}^{4+} \rightarrow \mathrm{Ti}^{3+}$ , and  $\mathrm{V}^{3+} \rightarrow \mathrm{V}^{2+}$ , respectively. By taking advantage of the distinct redox couples between  $\mathrm{V}^{3+} / \mathrm{V}^{4+}$  and  $\mathrm{Ti}^{4+} / \mathrm{Ti}^{3+}$ , a symmetric SIB using  $\mathrm{Na}_{2} \mathrm{VTi}(\mathrm{PO}_{4})_{3}$  as both cathode and anode demonstrates an ultralong lifetime over 10000 cycles, as shown in Figure 17i. Similarly, Dou and co-workers have successfully synthesized a rhombohedral structured two-phase  $\mathrm{Na}_{2} \mathrm{LiV}_{2}(\mathrm{PO}_{4})_{3} / \mathrm{C}$  nanocomposite and employed it as both cathode and anode materials. $^{167}$  The resulting symmetric SIB exhibits excellent electrochemical performance, including good cycling stability with capacity retention of  $71.1\%$  and initial capacity of  $87.6 \mathrm{mAh} \mathrm{g}^{-1}$  at  $1 \mathrm{C}$  after 100 cycles. It is imperative to mention that the assembly of symmetric cells is conducive to simplifying the preparation of electrode and reducing the costs. Therefore, the symmetric SIBs have bright prospects for the furtherance of SIBs.

(c) Rate capability and corresponding cycle performance (inset) of  $\mathrm{Na_2C_6O_6}$ . (d) Cycle retention of  $\mathrm{Na_2C_6O_6}$  electrode at  $500\mathrm{mA g^{-1}}$  and the corresponding voltage profile (inset) for 50 cycles. (e) Evolution of voltage profiles of  $\mathrm{Na_2C_6O_6}$  electrode during sequential changes of charge cutoff voltages from  $2.9\mathrm{V}$  (1-2 cycles) to  $3.35\mathrm{V}$  (3-4 cycles). ![](images/93a1b5410bde0f7bd3a37ac1dfad4824f195a9a490c4c862152eaba37fc464d9.jpg)

PBAs have also been investigated as alternative cathode materials to the conventional layered and polyanionic compounds in recent years because of their large ion channels, low element cost, nontoxicity, and easy synthesis at room temperature. $^{140,168,169}$ $\mathrm{KM}^{\mathrm{II}}\mathrm{Fe}^{\mathrm{III}}(\mathrm{CN})_6$  ( $\mathrm{M} = \mathrm{Mn}$ , Fe, Co, Ni, and Zn) compounds as PBAs were introduced as cathodes for nonaqueous SIBs. $^{170}$  The electrode with a  $\mathrm{Fe}^{3+}/\mathrm{Fe}^{2+}$  redox couple and a single voltage plateau at  $3.0\mathrm{V}$  vs.  $\mathrm{Na}^{+}/\mathrm{Na}$  delivers a reversible capacity of about  $60\mathrm{mAh}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$ . However, the key problems for the PBA-based SIBs include their insufficient cycle life and low EE in nonaqueous electrolytes, which are attributed to the low electrical conductivity and structural imperfection. $^{136}$  Similarly, Zhang and co-workers have conducted an important study on designing and preparing  $\mathrm{FeFe(CN)}_6$  nanoparticles on a flexible carbon fiber paper as a binder-free cathode by using low

temperature strategies. $^{171}$  The designed electrode structure with a highly conductive scaffold effectively utilizes all the active mass and enhances electrical contact. This results in excellent electrochemical performance of the SIB, including good rate capability (62 mAh g $^{-1}$  at 5 C) and long-term cycling life with 81.2% capacity retention at 1 C over 1000 cycles.

Organic compounds that can be obtained from natural biomass with minimal energy consumption are attractive low-cost and sustainable choices for battery electrode materials. These compounds provide high energy density and long cycling stability.[172] Tarascon and co-workers first reported  $\mathrm{Li}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  in 2008, exhibiting a theoretical capacity of  $560\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  based on four-electron redox chemistry in LIBs.[173] However,  $\mathrm{Li}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  showed poor cycle stability due to its dissolution and exfoliation, which limits its practical applications.[174] The research work on

![](images/4a93a7ed79dd41667fee22dc3d47f4a1111c1f9e851079f58d8bb6ac117d935a.jpg)

![](images/053e1b118420b072e3f3551092809e8cfb8e54b8edaa05c5afca1482353e8df6.jpg)

Figure 19. Typical examples of carbon materials as anodes for PIBs. (a) Schematic illustration of the preparation process for the PCMs. (b) TEM image, HR-TEM image (inset is the corresponding SAED pattern), and EDS mappings of PCMs. (c) Charge/discharge profiles of PCMs in the 2nd, 3rd, 5th, 10th, 50th, and 100th at  $50\mathrm{mA}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$ . (d) Long-term cycle stability and CE of PCMs at a high current density of  $1000\mathrm{mA}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 187. Copyright 2018 Wiley-VCH. ![](images/34299c864c0e758ca359a6331d8ded4a36ab4bce044d16c87d9395c16c64b4ba.jpg)

$\mathrm{Li}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  has led to investigation of  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$ , which demonstrates excellent cycle stability in SIBs.[175] Although it seems intuitive to expect a similar four-electron redox reaction in  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$ , a substantial capacity loss with lower reversible capacity than its theoretical capacity of  $501\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  has been observed instead. In order to address this shortcoming, Bao and co-workers have improved the electrochemical performance of  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  and provided an effective reaction pathway to achieve a reversible four-electron redox reaction.[176] The reversible phase transformation of  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  accompanied by spontaneous nanostructure formation of the active particles was achieved by decreasing the size of the active particles and selecting proper electrolytes. Structurally,  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  is comprised of hexagonally packed  $\mathrm{Na}^+$  cations, which are alternately placed above  $\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6^{2-}$  at a distance of  $a/4$  (Figure 18a). The obtained  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  maintains its uniform nanostructure within a few hundred nanometers (Figure 18b). To understand the sodiation

mechanism of  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  material, the electrochemical performance has been subjected to further testing. As shown in Figure 18c, a reversible capacity of  $498\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  is obtained at  $50\mathrm{mA}$ $\mathrm{g}^{-1}$  in Nano/DEGDME, which is equivalent to  $95\%$  of its theoretical capacity. Moreover, even at very high rates of  $500\mathrm{mA}$ $\mathrm{g}^{-1}$  and  $1000\mathrm{mA}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$ , the electrode retained specific capacities of 408 and  $371\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$ , respectively. In addition, the  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  electrode showed good capacity retention of  $90.8\%$  at  $500\mathrm{mA}$ $\mathrm{g}^{-1}$  after 50 cycles (Figure 18d). As shown in Figure 18e, the characteristic charge plateau is observed at  $\sim 3\mathrm{V}$ , corresponding to its phase transformation from  $\gamma \text{-Na}_{2.5}\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  to  $\alpha \text{-Na}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  phase. The parallel nanostructures are aligned with the voltage profiles obtained with the higher discharge cutoff at  $1\mathrm{V}$ . The full cell assembled with a precycled P@C anode and an electrochemically sodiated  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{C}_6\mathrm{O}_6$  cathode exhibits a reversible capacity of  $265\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  (energy density of  $281\mathrm{Whkg^{-1}}$ ) at  $50\mathrm{mA}$ $\mathrm{g}^{-1}$  based on the total mass of cathode and anode (Figure

Figure 20. Typical examples of P materials as anodes for PIBs. (a) Schematic illustration of preparation of  $\mathrm{P@TBMC}$  composite. (b) SEM image with the corresponding EDS elemental mapping and line-scanning of  $\mathrm{P@TBMC-2.4}$ . (c) Discharge/charge voltage profiles at different cycles of  $\mathrm{P@TBMC-2.4}$  anode for PIBs. (d) Long-term cycling performance at  $0.5\mathrm{A g}^{-1}$  after the initial two-cycle activation at  $0.05\mathrm{A g}^{-1}$  of  $\mathrm{P@TBMC-2.4}$  anode for PIBs. ![](images/6693b6349e29e817591377bcc7c395470c67efd1ba10f7c9caa855b0ca98b2ae.jpg)

18f). Therefore, it can be established that the structural diversity and tunable properties of the organic molecules provide good opportunities to modulate Na storage potentials and reversible capacities of the organic electrodes. This however is achieved by manipulating different functional groups, morphologies, and surface coating. Last but not least, altering substituted functional groups on the conjugated carboxylate organic molecules is a feasible way to change the thermodynamic and kinetic properties of the organic electrodes.

Despite all the challenges, the first-generation SIBs offer promising alternatives to LIBs and therefore are already attracting commercial interest for a wide variety of energy storage applications. Moreover, most of the research effort has been focused on electrode active materials, electrolytes, binders, current collectors, and other cell components for ensuring a prosperous future for this technology. However, further grid

scale applications of SIBs are not just based on performance indicators such as gravimetric and volumetric energy densities, gravimetric and volumetric power densities, cycle and calendar life, and charge time but also on their safety, sustainability, and cost effectiveness.

# 3.5. Potassium-lon Batteries

Recently, potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) have emerged as another possible energy storage system because of the abundance of potassium resources in the Earth's crust and in oceans, similar to that of sodium. $^{177,178}$  In addition, the  $\mathrm{K}^{+}/\mathrm{K}$ $(-2.93\mathrm{~V}$  vs. SHE) redox couple has a lower standard redox potential than  $\mathrm{Na}^{+}/\mathrm{Na}$ $(-2.71\mathrm{~V}$  vs. SHE), close to that of  $\mathrm{Li}^{+}/$  Li  $(-3.04\mathrm{~V}$  vs. SHE). The standard redox potential of the  $\mathrm{K}^{+}/\mathrm{K}$  redox couple leads to a potentially high operating voltage and energy density for PIBs. $^{179}$  The most important advantage of

PIBs compared with SIBs is that graphite can accommodate reversible  $\mathrm{K}^+$  deintercalation/intercalation. $^{178}$  Given these upsides, PIBs have rapidly attracted considerable interest, not to mention that various materials have been developed and evaluated as potential electrodes of PIBs. $^{180}$  The testing techniques and materials selection for LIBs are mostly applicable for PIBs. However, the ionic radius of  $\mathrm{K}^+$  (0.138 nm) is larger than those of  $\mathrm{Li}^+$  (0.076 nm) and  $\mathrm{Na}^+$  (0.102 nm), which leads to sluggish reaction kinetics and poor cycling stability in PIBs. $^{181}$  Thus, efficient anode and cathode materials with high capacity and long cycling stability are highly desirable to promote further development of PIBs for GSES applications. Similar to LIBs and SIBs, PIBs contain all the functional battery configurations including anode, organic electrolyte, separator, cathode, and current collectors. The only characteristic that distinguishes PIBs from LIBs or SIBs is the transfer kinetics of  $\mathrm{K}^+$  rather than  $\mathrm{Li}^+$  and  $\mathrm{Na}^+$ . The commonly known anode materials for PIBs include hard carbon, K intercalation compounds, K metal-alloying-reaction compounds, K conversion-reaction compounds, and organic compounds. $^{178,182}$  In contrast, the most promising cathode materials mainly include PBA, layered compounds, polyanions, and organic materials. $^{180}$  In this section, we present an overview of recent research on PIBs with exclusive emphasis on the development of anode and cathode materials.

3.5.1. Anode Materials for PIBs. In addition to graphite anode, which delivers a considerable capacity when employed in PIBs, large numbers of anode materials including carbon materials, metals and alloys, metal oxides, sulfides, and phosphides, and carbon-based composite materials have been investigated. $^{178,183}$  Numerous studies have mainly concentrated on the development of carbon materials, although carbon anodes in PIBs have previously suffered from insufficient cycle life and poor rate capability owing to the influence of the large  $\mathrm{K}^+$  ionic radius. $^{178}$  Recently, the carbon materials based anodes have made remarkable progress with novel structures. In this regard, Xu and co-workers synthesized a free-standing porous CNF paper by electrospinning and carbonization, whereas Yu and co-workers have reported a quasi-two-dimensional core-shell nanostructured carbon nanoplate as anodes for PIBs $^{184,185}$ . Upon electrochemical cycling, both of the anode materials show reasonable charge/discharge rate and long cycling. In addition, doping heteroatoms into various carbon forms is another effective strategy to introduce defects, which are responsible for increasing the adsorption energy of  $\mathrm{K}^+$  in carbon materials, eventually leading to the enhanced performance of PIBs. $^{186}$  Yang and co-workers recently reported a class of S and O codoped porous carbon microspheres (PCMs) as novel anodes for PIBs. The proposed PCMs are synthesized through the pyrolysis of polymer microspheres composed of a liquid crystal/epoxy monomer/thiol hardener system, as shown in Figure 19a. $^{187}$  The transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and high-resolution TEM (HR-TEM) micrographs and energy disperse spectroscopy (EDS) mapping in Figure 19b illustrate the porous morphology and amorphous nature of the PCMs. Figure 19c shows typical charge/discharge curves of the hard carbon PCMs. A voltage plateau well above the plating potential of K metal is observed, which inhibits the formation of K metal dendrites. The PCM based PIBs deliver a highly stable capacity of  $108.4\mathrm{mAh}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$  after 2000 cycles at  $1000\mathrm{mA}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$ , as shown in Figure 19d. Similarly, Tang and co-workers successfully synthesized carbon nanosheets doped with an ultrahigh content (22.7 atomic wt %) of nitrogen (UNCNs) as an anode material for PIBs (Figure

19e). The resulting PIB delivers excellent cycling performance with capacity retention of  $70\%$  after 3000 cycles at a high current density of  $5\mathrm{Ag}^{-1}$  (Figure 19f).<sup>188</sup> Furthermore, Qian and coworkers have employed a low-cost and large-scale method to fabricate phosphorus-doped hard carbon (PHC-700) by crosslinking phosphoric acid and epoxy resin followed by annealing at  $700^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .<sup>189</sup> The PHC-700 anode based PIBs exhibit a reversible capacity of  $381.9\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  at  $0.1\mathrm{Ag}^{-1}$  and capacity of  $260\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  after 1000 cycles at  $0.2\mathrm{Ag}^{-1}$ .

Considering the chemical stability of different phosphorus allotropes (white P, red P, and black P), red P is the most promising anode for PIBs. However, the cyclic performance of the red P anode is extremely poor because of the huge volume change of P during the alloying/dealloying process, which results in cracking and pulverization of P. In addition, the low electrical conductivity of red P drastically reduces the capacities of PIBs during fast charge/discharge. To solve these problems, it is necessary to choose a highly conductive matrix to alleviate the volume change of red P during cycling and enhance electrical conductivity of the electrode. To solve this problem,  $\mathrm{Qu}$  and coworkers designed and synthesized a mesoporous carbon material with a carbon nanotube (CNT)-backbone (TBMC) and impregnated it with red P, finally forming a  $\mathrm{P@TBMC}$  composite (Figure 20a). It is evident in Figure 20b that the highly porous structure is visible on the surface of  $\mathrm{P@TBMC-2.4}$  with no trace of P particles, demonstrating that  $\mathrm{P}$  is completely encapsulated within the pores and homogeneously distributed in the composite. When assembled in a PIB, the electrode delivers initial discharge/charge capacities of  $772.8 / 490.9\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  with an initial CE of  $63.5\%$ . In the second cycle, however, the CE reaches  $90.4\%$  with discharge/charge capacities of  $527.8 / 477.0\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  (Figure 20c). Furthermore, the  $\mathrm{P@TBMC}$  anode exhibits superior electrochemical performance by delivering a stable capacity of  $244\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at  $0.5\mathrm{A g^{-1}}$  for 200 cycles (Figure 20d). Similarly, Yu and co-workers have designed a structure of red P embedded into free-standing nitrogen-doped porous hollow CNFs (red  $\mathrm{P@N-PHCNFs}$ ). The scanning transmission electron microscopy (STEM) images and EDS elemental mapping of the red  $\mathrm{P@N-PHCNFs}$  are shown in Figure 20e-h, indicating the homogeneous distribution of red P and the N element doping into the N-PHCNF matrix. As shown in Figure 20i, the red  $\mathrm{P@N-PHCNF}$  anode with large surface area and high pore volume effectively alleviates the large volume expansion and maintains superior structural stability. Consequently, the red  $\mathrm{P@N-PHCNF}$  anode based PIBs show outstanding rate capability ( $745\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at 0.1 A g $^{-1}$  and  $342\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at  $5\mathrm{A g^{-1}}$ ) (Figure 20j). Furthermore, the batteries exhibit long cycle life with high reversible capacities ( $533\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at  $1\mathrm{A g^{-1}}$  after 200 cycles, 465 and  $282\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at 2 and  $5\mathrm{A g^{-1}}$  after 800 cycles, respectively; Figure 20k). Although the  $\mathrm{P}$  delivers high theoretical specific capacity, the structural stability still needs alteration, for instance, with functional coatings composed of other elements or materials.

In addition to the allotropes of P, Sn is another promising anode material for energy storage of PIBs due to its nontoxicity, crustal abundance, and cost effectiveness.[182] However, unlike SIBs, the alloying reaction of metallic Sn with K produces little theoretical specific capacity of  $225\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  and large volume change.[182] In this respect, Guo and co-workers employed a  $\mathrm{Sn_4P_3 / C}$  composite as a novel composite electrode for PIBs.[193] This composite consolidates the advantages of Sn/C composites and the high capacity of P. Compared with P/C and Sn/C electrodes, the  $\mathrm{Sn_4P_3 / C}$  composite based electrode shows much

![](images/0ad14e78ccfa71fa8a26b22ce78371aab390da340772824272859479cd0fe3a0.jpg)

![](images/657514f2b21e3ba426378f6e4d2274b2fe1af9283d77719e04836acf7975cec4.jpg)

![](images/c806711465c84259c4bfbd868d8a69122c57eaff3cecd65f14592aa47b1f89a6.jpg)

![](images/2904e312e5d86d8364fc5f6061c3df65bfaa729ddd6160a2c469eb4efce31ad5.jpg)

Inset is high magnification SEM image. (c) Corresponding elemental mapping. (d) Electrochemical charge/discharge curves of s-KFMO cathode at a constant current of  $20\mathrm{mA}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$ . ![](images/718581455e9e980d9cb5e64e1e271c7752312b8114bebd06545d47ea23ff7b5d.jpg)

better cycling performance by delivering a retained capacity of  $307.2\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at  $50~\mathrm{mA~g^{-1}}$  after 50 cycles. It is important to mention that Sb also is a promising anode material due to its low reaction potential and high theoretical capacity (660 mAh  $\mathrm{g}^{-1}$ ).<sup>182</sup> However, a general problem for alloy anodes is their large volume change of  $\sim 300\%$  during the potassiation/depotassiation process, which usually causes rapid capacity fade and hence low CE.<sup>194</sup> In this regard, an efficient method is to employ an Sb-carbon composite anode to decrease the capacity degradation of the cell. Therefore, Kim and co-workers reported a composite electrode composed of Sb nanoparticles, amorphous carbon, and RGO, showing stable cycling for 100 cycles (79% retention).<sup>195</sup> Further, Qian and co-workers have also investigated nanoporous structural Zn-Sb alloy as a PIB anode, which is prepared by evaporating high-boiling-point materials to obtain a pure high-boiling-point sample.<sup>196</sup> The principle advantage of Zn-Sb alloy is its ability to accommodate volume expansion and accelerate ion transport, delivering a longer cycling life with capacity retention of 62.35% after 50 cycles and a higher rate capacity of  $265\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at  $500\mathrm{mA~g^{-1}}$  than the bulk-Sb anode. Therefore, the development of high-capacity alloy materials is essential in maintaining the structural stability and reducing the volume expansion of anodes in PIB systems.

3.5.2. Cathode Materials for PIBs. The cathode materials for PIBs generally include organic materials, PBAs, layered transition metal oxides, and polyanionic compounds, which are similar to those for SIBs. Organic electrodes provide a new avenue to develop PIBs with high energy densities. In addition, organic materials are more accessible and synthesized from cheap chemicals, offering a promising avenue to low-cost PIBs for LSES.[197] Among numerous studies, Hu and co-workers have designed and fabricated a nonaqueous PIB by employing 3,4,9,10-perylene tetracarboxylic acid dianhydride (PTCDA) as the cathode, which had been previously studied as an SIB cathode.[198,199] The PTCDA electrode exhibits a high capacity of  $131\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  and great cycling performance, with a capacity retention of  $66.1\%$  over 200 cycles. In addition, this cathode material shows the same electrochemical performance as SIBs.[199] Similarly, Wang and co-workers reported poly(pentacenetetrone sulfide) (PPTS) as a new organic cathode for PIBs.[179] The PPTS cathode exhibits fast discharge/charge ability  $(160\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  at a current density of  $10\mathrm{A g}^{-1}$ ) and long cycle life (capacity higher than  $190\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  even after 3000 cycles at  $5\mathrm{A g}^{-1}$ ). It is therefore of particular significance to explore new organic cathodes for PIBs with high capacity, cycling stability, and rate performance.

Layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compounds have also been reported as cathodes for PIBs due to their fast

![](images/fbc91588d348fadba9ec06ba360f1de08fc5b486eadbd2c63716ba18a53a1783.jpg)  
a

Figure 22. Typical examples of PBAs as cathode materials for PIBs. (a) XRD Rietveld refinement pattern for the KFeMnHCF-3565 sample. The inset is the SEM image of the KFeMnHCF-3565 sample. (b) Typical structure of  $\mathrm{K}_x\mathrm{Fe}_y\mathrm{Mn}_{1 - y}[\mathrm{Fe}(\mathrm{CN})_6]_w.z\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  in the  $P21 / n$  space group. (c, d) Charge/ discharge curves of the 1st, 10th, and 40th cycles at  $10\mathrm{C}$  for the KFeMnHCF-3565 electrode in (c)  $1\mathrm{M}$  and (d)  $22\mathrm{M}$ $\mathrm{KCF}_3\mathrm{SO}_3$  electrolytes. (e) Rate capability and long-term cycling performance of the KFeMnHCF-3565 electrode from 0 to  $1.3\mathrm{V}$  (vs.  $\mathrm{Ag / AgCl}$ ) in  $22\mathrm{M}$ $\mathrm{KCF}_3\mathrm{SO}_3$  electrolyte.  $1\mathrm{C} = 0.13\mathrm{Ag}^{-1}$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 210. Copyright 2019 Springer Nature.

development in LIBs and SIBs. Pomerantseva and co-workers introduced  $\delta -\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5$  as a cathode selection in organic PIBs, which exhibited high initial discharge capacity of  $268\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at a current rate of C/50 and great capacity retention of  $74\%$  after 50 cycles at a constant current of C/15.[200]  $\delta -\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5$  has also been reported as a high capacity cathode material for SIBs.[201] Also, a novel fluorophosphate cathode  $\mathrm{K_3V_2(PO_4)_2F_3}$  derived from  $\mathrm{Na}_3\mathrm{V}_2(\mathrm{PO}_4)_2\mathrm{F}_3$ , when employed in PIBs, delivers a capacity of over  $100\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  and energy density of around  $400\mathrm{Whkg^{-1}}$ .[202] Layered transition metal oxide cathodes have been considered for PIBs due to their high theoretical capacities, good structural stability, low cost, and environmental friendliness.[203] Ceder and co-workers have investigated highly reversible layered  $\mathrm{K_{0.5}MnO_2}$  and  $\mathrm{K}_{0.6}\mathrm{CoO}_2$  cathodes.[203,204] However, these cathodes yield low energy density and poor cycling life and therefore cannot meet practical energy storage demands. Therefore, new materials and structural design for layered transition metal oxide materials are required to facilitate  $\mathbf{K}^{+}$  reaction kinetics.

Zhang and co-workers fabricated layered P2-type hierarchical  $\mathrm{K}_{0.65}\mathrm{Fe}_{0.5}\mathrm{Mn}_{0.5}\mathrm{O}_2$  (P2-KFMO) microspheres via a modified solvent-thermal method.[205] As shown in Figure 21a-c, these secondary microspheres assembled from primary nanoparticles are compact, robust, and capable of reducing volume change in  $\mathbf{K}^{+}$ intercalation/deintercalation and accelerating the diffusion kinetics of  $\mathbf{K}^{+}$ . When assembled in PIBs, these P2-KFMO microspheres show highly reversible K storage capacity of 151 mAh g $^{-1}$  at 20 mA g $^{-1}$  and long cycling stability with 78% capacity retention after 350 cycles (Figure 21d,e). As K metal is much more reactive than Li metal and Na metal, PIBs using P2-KFMO as the cathode and hard carbon as the anode are more practical choices (Figure 21f). As shown in Figure 21g, the PIB full cell delivers considerable discharge capacity of 75 mAh g $^{-1}$  at a current density of 100 mAh g $^{-1}$  and average CE of over 99% during charge/discharge operation. Moreover, the s-KFMO/ hard carbon based PIB retains >80% of initial capacity after 100 cycles. Similarly, Wang and co-workers have introduced

$\mathrm{K}_{1.39}\mathrm{Mn}_3\mathrm{O}_6$  microspheres as cathode materials for PIBs.[206] An effective  $\mathrm{AlF}_3$  surface coating strategy was applied to change the surface structure and improve the electrochemical performance of  $\mathrm{K}_{1.39}\mathrm{Mn}_3\mathrm{O}_6$  microspheres. The aforementioned cathode delivers reasonable capacity (about  $110\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  at  $10\mathrm{mA g}^{-1}$ ) and excellent cycling stability over 100 cycles with a capacity retention of  $94.9\%$ , thereby outperforming uncoated microspheres or their bulk counterpart. Therefore, it is an efficient method from the perspectives of the electrode structure and new materials to constitute a cathode with high energy density and long cycle for PIBs.

The traditional open-framework based PBAs have attracted much attention as PIB cathode materials for providing plausible ion channels for  $\mathrm{K}^+$  redox kinetics. $^{169}$  For example, Cui and coworkers have designed and synthesized nickel hexacyanoferrate (NiHCF) electrode materials in bulk quantities by the coprecipitation strategy, for delivering good cycling stability and high rate capability in PIBs. $^{207}$  Similarly, Wang and coworkers reported high-potassium-ion-content potassium iron-II ferrocyanide dehydrate nanocubes as cathodes for aqueous PIBs, which exhibit high capacity and fast kinetics. $^{208}$  Following this investigation, Zhao and co-workers reported a uniform mesoporous potassium-rich nickel ferrocyanide (KNiFC) cathode for ultrafast aqueous PIBs. $^{209}$  The KNiFC with large channel sizes exhibits fast  $\mathrm{K}^+$  insertion/extraction with an ultrafast rate performance within 4.1 s at 500 C. However, the KNiFC based PIB yields low capacity, less than  $80\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$ . In addition, Hu and co-workers have proposed a novel Fe-substituted Mn-rich PBA  $\mathrm{K_xFe_yMn_{1 - y}[Fe(CN)_6]_w\cdot zH_2O}$  (KFeMnHCF) cathode. $^{210}$  This cathode material is characterized by its monoclinic phase with a space group of  $P21 / n$  (Figure 22a) and crystal structure (Figure 22b) comprising a typical open framework with N-coordinated Mn or Fe cations and C-coordinated Fe cations. The SEM image of KFeMnHCF indicates that both samples possess a cubic morphology with edge length of  $200 - 800\mathrm{nm}$  (inset of Figure 22a). Upon assembly in a PIB and cycling, the KFeMnHCF-3565 electrode retains  $60\%$  capacity in the  $1\mathrm{M}$ $\mathrm{KCF}_3\mathrm{SO}_3$  dilute electrolyte (Figure 22c). When the electrolyte concentration is increased from 1 to  $22\mathrm{M}$ , the KFeMnHCF-3565 electrode shows significant improvement in its cycling stability with no capacity or voltage decay in the initial 40 cycles (Figure 22d). The elemental analysis results of the electrolyte after 40 cycles shown in the inset confirmed that the KFeMnHCF-3565 electrode experienced severe dissolution of Fe and Mn during cycling in dilute electrolyte but did not undergo dissolution in concentrated electrolyte. This indicates that it is extremely important to utilize highly concentrated electrolyte to stabilize the electrodes of PIBs. Furthermore, Figure 22e illustrates the long-term cycling stability of the KFeMnHCF-3565 electrode, exhibiting a high capacity of  $94\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at an ultrahigh rate of  $100\mathrm{C}$  and  $90\%$  capacity retention over 10000 cycles when tested from 10 to  $120\mathrm{C}$ . Remarkably, even after 10000 cycles at  $100\mathrm{C}$ , the cell still achieves capacity up to  $128\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  when the current rate is set back to  $10\mathrm{C}$ , demonstrating its robust structural stability (Figure 22e). Therefore, an excellent framework structure for PBA cathodes is critical to develop high performance PIBs for GSES.

# 3.6. Zinc-Ion Batteries

Compared with alkali metals (Li, Na, and K), the metallic Zn possesses a higher redox potential  $(-0.76\mathrm{V}$  vs. SHE) and water compatibility.[211] In addition, aqueous electrolytes are more

advantageous than the organic electrolytes for zinc-ion batteries (ZIBs) thanks to their lower cost, better safety, higher ionic conductivity, and greener environmental impact.[212] Therefore, the aqueous ZIBs (AZIBs) have been considered as promising alternatives for LSES applications.[213] Zn metal is commonly used as the anode in AZIBs, due to its high gravimetric capacity  $(820\mathrm{mAh}\mathrm{g}^{-1})$  and suitable potential.[214] However, the corrosion and formation of Zn dendrites hinder the further development of ZIBs.[215] Some effective mitigation strategies have been reported to suppress the corrosion and dendritic formation of Zn anodes. Typically, a good protection layer on the Zn metal has been proven to be an effective strategy for restricting dendrite growth. Recently, an ultrathin  $\mathrm{TiO}_2$  film and nanoporous  $\mathrm{CaCO}_3$  coating have been demonstrated to achieve long life for ZIBs.[216,217] Further, 3D framework structures have also been reported to eliminate the dendrite formation by large surface areas.[218] Furthermore, electrolyte additives such as diethyl ether are conducive in stabilizing the solid-liquid interface in ZIBs and suppressing the dendrite formation on Zn anode.[219] However, it is hard to find an excellent cathode material for facilitating the intercalation/deintercalation of  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}$  due to the high polarization of  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}$  as well as their narrow voltage range as a consequence of water splitting in the AZIBs.[220] The development on AZIB cathode materials is still in the preliminary stage.[221] Some cathode materials have been explored as the zinc-ion hosts and are generally divided into Mn-based materials,[79,222,223] V-based materials,[224-226] PBAs,[227] organic materials,[228,229] and others (e.g.,  $\mathrm{Na}_3\mathrm{V}_2(\mathrm{PO}_4)_3$ ,[230] VS,[231] and MoS,[232]). The characteristics of different cathode materials have been summarized in Table 6. In this section, we mainly recap the recent development of the most extensively studied Mn-based and V-based materials for ZIBs.

Table 6. Characteristics of Different Cathode Materials for ZIBs  ${}^{a}$  

<table><tr><td>material</td><td>advantages</td><td>shortcomings</td></tr><tr><td>Mn-based materials</td><td>high energy density</td><td>Mn dissolution resulting in capacity fading</td></tr><tr><td>V-based materials</td><td>high specific power, good cycling stability</td><td>low operation voltage, low specific capacity</td></tr><tr><td>PBAs</td><td>high operation voltages</td><td>low CE of the initial cycles, poor cycling stability</td></tr><tr><td>organic materials</td><td>long cycle stability</td><td>low power density</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">aReproduced with permission from ref 79. Copyright 2019 Wiley-VCH.</td></tr></table>

3.6.1. Mn-Based Cathodes for ZIBs. Mn-based cathodes have been widely investigated for ZIBs, especially the manganese oxides (e.g.,  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$ ) due to their low cost, crustal abundance, and environmental friendliness. Particularly, the  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  cathode has a high theoretical capacity ( $308\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  based on single electron transfer between  $\mathrm{Mn}^{4+}$  and  $\mathrm{Mn}^{3+}$ ) and high voltages ( $0.8-1.8\mathrm{V}$ ).<sup>79</sup> In general, there are various  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  polymorphs, including hollandite ( $\alpha$ - $\mathrm{MnO}_2$ ), pyrolusite ( $\beta$ - $\mathrm{MnO}_2$ ), ramsdellite ( $\gamma$ - $\mathrm{MnO}_2$ ), romanechite ( $\delta$ - $\mathrm{MnO}_2$ ), hexagonal ( $\varepsilon$ - $\mathrm{MnO}_2$ ), todorokite, and amorphous  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$ , which can be employed as the hosts for  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}$ .<sup>79</sup> These structural variants of  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  have different roles in the redox reaction mechanism, which dictates electrochemical performance of ZIBs.<sup>79</sup> In 2012, Kang and coworkers used  $\alpha$ - $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  as cathode, Zn metal as anode, and mild zinc salt solution as aqueous electrolyte, to build an aqueous  $\mathrm{Zn}/\mathrm{MnO}_2$  battery.<sup>214</sup> Despite of the high CE of the battery, its

![](images/90055f1ecf534187618899b8bf7ce0c4fdaf0fa1602eeed4595eaeb3b899fd80.jpg)

![](images/82207bd469c38160ec6349c4fa66edfc6e1afed6cab3f3be537789600954fe99.jpg)

![](images/12772db77ef63c854a4ff0f53e5a16074a003c4172642195ec76b560a62ad4d9.jpg)

![](images/364224416fc77313ac464ccb2b69fddb3a71e4b2ef7994595931205f540325d1.jpg)

![](images/7f2fc4d938e2b340c7aa46670fc5d5f7d1bc28a8bd03019ede309a04f51d0237.jpg)

![](images/22c08ed110bbb3e38f377532dc24474f5ade3fd4457a6e895b62638b48a51c58.jpg)  
Figure 23. Typical examples of  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  batteries for improving cycling stability and operational voltage with the addition of  $\mathrm{CF}_3\mathrm{SO}_3^-$ . Schematic illustration of (a) primary alkaline  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery using KOH electrolyte and (b) rechargeable  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  cell using  $\mathrm{CF}_3\mathrm{SO}_3^-$ -based electrolyte. (c) Comparison of the cycling performance of  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  cells with different electrolytes of  $45\mathrm{wt}\%$  KOH at  $0.32\mathrm{C}$  or  $3\mathrm{M}\mathrm{ZnSO}_4$ ,  $3\mathrm{M}\mathrm{Zn}(\mathrm{CF}_3\mathrm{SO}_3)_2$  or  $3\mathrm{M}\mathrm{Zn}(\mathrm{CF}_3\mathrm{SO}_3)_2$  with  $0.1\mathrm{M}\mathrm{Mn}(\mathrm{CF}_3\mathrm{SO}_3)_2$  additive at  $0.65\mathrm{C}$  ( $1\mathrm{C} = 308\mathrm{mA}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$ ). (d) Charge/discharge profiles at different rates and (e) long-cycle performance at  $6.5\mathrm{C}$  for  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  cells in  $3\mathrm{M}\mathrm{Zn}(\mathrm{CF}_3\mathrm{SO}_3)_2$  with  $0.1\mathrm{M}\mathrm{Mn}(\mathrm{CF}_3\mathrm{SO}_3)_2$  additive. Inset shows the capacity evolution in the initial 19 cycles. (f) Digital photograph of the soft-package battery powering a series of LEDs. (g) Cycling performance of the soft-package battery at a constant current of  $0.72\mathrm{A}$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 236. Copyright 2017 Springer Nature.

![](images/b78ffdbdb1e21e2005cec29f3d75169bf21161b7a1111f0102513736e31490ce.jpg)

cycling stability has not been up to the mark. Generally, the  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  materials have common problems in terms of poor electrical conductivity and large volume expansion, which severely affect the rate and cycle performance for ZIBs. To solve the problems, recent research has concentrated on structural modification of Mn-based materials. For example, Choi and co-workers have designed a novel layered manganese oxide based ZIB cathode with high content of crystal water, which can effectively restrain the effect between  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}$  and the host framework for accelerating  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}$  diffusion.[233] This cathode material delivers a high reversible capacity with decent cycling and rate performance. Similarly, Kang and co-workers put forward the idea of mesoporous  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  flower-like nanospheres as cathodes for ZIBs, delivering a high rate capacity of  $124\mathrm{mAh}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$  at  $3.0\mathrm{A}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$  and excellent cycling stability over 2000 cycles.[223] In addition, the structures of N-doped porous

framework and hierarchical nanoflower in manganese oxide have exhibited excellent electrochemical performances.[221,234] Therefore, the good structures for Mn-based materials have immense effect in enhancing the electrochemical performance for ZIBs cathodes.

In addition to the manganese oxide based ZIB cathodes, studies have emphasized the development of electrolytes for exploring high-performance  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  batteries. Apropos this, Liu and co-workers have reported the utility of  $\mathrm{ZnSO_4}$  with a  $\mathrm{MnSO_4}$  additive as aqueous electrolyte for  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery.[235] The  $\mathrm{MnSO_4}$  additive in electrolyte improves the cycling stability of the  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery by suppressing the dissolution of  $\mathrm{Mn^{2 + }}$  in the aqueous solution. With this additive, the  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery exhibits excellent rate capacity and cycling stability. In another study, Chen and co-workers employed  $\mathrm{Zn(CF_3SO_3)_2}$  salt with a  $\mathrm{Mn(CF_3SO_3)_2}$  additive in

![](images/dd457b9ee2f4822603b21fec7fccaa7d55274082bc85022220a88c33e7a67e48.jpg)

![](images/7cf73300ea82df8fab2e5fb37099298e65cbd7e3d75da2f091cea3488a4d70fa.jpg)

![](images/e36328f863c487d39fd9d802ba94b884fd190c4dddcc0b75535b422ef3f63c6d.jpg)

![](images/82ce2bc2cebdde4e09ea41512152f2d903824e77748d9f122e4ea69704b42eb9.jpg)

![](images/f670283484c06ec38c855bfea110732aa8d696c6a6d030d46743b494eae219fc.jpg)  
Figure 24. Typical examples of  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  batteries with cathode  $\mathrm{Mn^{2 + } / MnO_2}$  chemistry. (a) Configuration of a membrane-free aqueous electrolytic  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  redox-flow battery. (b) Charge/discharge curves at a constant voltage charge of  $2\mathrm{V}$  to  $0.5\mathrm{mAh}$  and galvanostatic discharge at  $4^{\circ}C$  to  $1.0\mathrm{V}$  and (c) corresponding capacity retention over 1000 cycles. (d) Digital photograph of the membrane-free  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery. Large capacity tests at  $2\mathrm{V}$  to  $1.2\mathrm{Ah}$  : (e) charge/discharge curves and (f) capacity retention over 500 cycles. Reproduced with permission from ref 237. Copyright 2020 WileyVCH.

![](images/1f7c561f0290b84fd9e19088c313e967a7cfa9d08c58af80c78bc948c0755206.jpg)

electrolyte for augmenting the operating voltage of  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery from 1.2 to  $1.35\mathrm{V}$ , which is higher than that of the alkaline counterpart, as shown in Figure 23a,b.[236] It has been further found that the additive  $\mathrm{Mn(CF_3SO_3)_2}$  can suppress  $\mathrm{Mn}^{2+}$  dissolution in the electrolyte and improve the cycling stability of  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  cell (Figure 23c). As a result, the designed  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery shows a high-rate capacity of  $100\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  even at a high rate of  $32.5\mathrm{C}$ , along with stable cycling and a capacity retention of  $94\%$  over 2000 cycles, as shown in Figure 23d,e. As for the performance, a typical assembled pouch cell lights up 44 LEDs with a stable discharge capacity of  $1550\mathrm{mAh}$  for 50 repeated cycles (Figure 23f,g). Furthermore, the  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  full cell delivers an energy density of  $158.5\mathrm{Whkg^{-1}}$  based on the total weight of the active materials.

In contrast to the prior studies reporting limited reversibility of solid-state  $\mathrm{MnO}_2 / \mathrm{MnOOH}$  cathode, Cui and co-workers have pioneered a novel aqueous rechargeable  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  flow battery based on dissolution-precipitation reactions in both cathode  $(\mathrm{Mn}^{2 + } / \mathrm{MnO}_2)$  and anode  $(\mathrm{Zn}^{2 + } / \mathrm{Zn})$  , involving mixing of anolyte and catholyte into one electrolyte, hence eliminating the need for an ion selective membrane.237 As shown in Figure

24a, the reaction mechanism of this membrane-free  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  flow battery mainly concentrates on the valence states of the cathode between  $\mathrm{Mn}^{4 + }$  and  $\mathrm{Mn}^{2 + }$ , which is completely different from the traditional  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  cell. The change of charge state of Mn from  $+4$  to  $+2$  in slightly acidic solution provides a high specific capacity up to  $616\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  and a high redox potential of  $1.23\mathrm{V}$ . Furthermore, the designed cell exhibits a well-defined discharge plateau of  $\sim 1.78\mathrm{V}$  with the initial CE of  $90\%$  (Figure 24b). More importantly, this aqueous  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  flow battery achieves excellent cycling stability with a high capacity retention of  $\sim 100\%$  over 1000 cycles at a discharge rate of  $4\mathrm{C}$  (Figure 24c). To further explore the advanced potential of this redox flow battery for GSES, the bench-scale cell of  $1.2\mathrm{Ah}$  demonstrates a discharge capacity of  $1.1\mathrm{Ah}$  with a CE of  $92.0\%$  (Figure 24d,e). Moreover, the cycling test shows that the CE keeps  $89.7\%$  after 500 cycles (Figure 24f), proving the possible longevity of this battery technology.

This particular  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery is expected to perform better in slightly acidic electrolytes.[222,237] In another investigation, Qiao and co-workers have designed a new electrolyte, comprising  $\mathrm{MnSO_4}$  and  $\mathrm{ZnSO_4}$  with a  $0.1\mathrm{MHz}_2\mathrm{SO}_4$  additive, for

![](images/e69974ac410f5b679a744b564964257efbab245ea6e68e7756b6026622228b72.jpg)

![](images/633cdc7a3f11b1fc6ed2749da8befcfe5989b0c309733e1dfc1ff8c20faf8a5a.jpg)

![](images/467b8f3c2bf0b3d25d45ec31ffbf911697a14de4c4d6ec70ec0d4aed62a6ed47.jpg)  
Figure 25. Advancements and applications of aqueous  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  batteries with the  $\mathrm{Mn^{2 + } / MnO_2}$  chemistry. (a) Schematic of the electrolytedecoupled  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery. (b) Schematic of the electrolyte-decoupled  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery with the introduction of  $\mathrm{Ni}^{2 + }$  into the electrolyte. (c) Long-term stability of a prototype membrane-free  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  flow battery at a charge capacity of  $1200\mathrm{mAh}$ . Inset is a digital photograph of a prototype lab scale-up  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  flow battery. (d) Discharge behavior of the lab-scale decoupled  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  batteries in two series-connected and two parallelconnected cells with a single cell capacity of  $3370\mathrm{mAh}$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 242. Copyright 2020 Wiley-VCH.

![](images/cadd28454a8e87eac35ed3f65214eb6a5aebee44b023cf4417a06a91091e72ba.jpg)

the aqueous  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery. $^{222}$  The addition of  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{SO}_4$  helps to reduce the  $\mathsf{pH}$  value of the electrolyte and increase the cathode potential. Upon electrochemical cycling, the designed  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery shows a high discharge plateau at about 1.95 V, and a high discharge current density of  $60\mathrm{mAcm}^{-2}$ . As for the Zn metal anode in alkaline electrolyte, it shows a low potential of  $-1.22\mathrm{V}$  vs. SHE. $^{238}$  Therefore, Liu and co-workers reported an electrolyte-decoupled  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery chemistry, demonstrating high voltage and high energy density using alkaline electrolyte in the anode and acidic electrolyte in the cathode with a bipolar membrane as the separator. $^{239}$  When such a  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  cell is subjected to reversible cycling, it delivers an operating voltage of  $2.44\mathrm{V}$ , which is higher than the traditional  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery. Furthermore, Hu and co-workers have designed another electrolyte-decoupled  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery using alkaline and acidic chambers separated by a neutral chamber, as shown in Figure 25a. $^{240}$  The battery has a high discharge plateau of about  $2.71\mathrm{V}$  at a current density of  $100\mathrm{mA}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$  and excellent rate performance. In addition, Qiao and co-workers reported an electrolyte-decoupled  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  cell with the cathode  $\mathrm{Mn^{2 + } / MnO_2}$  chemistry by introduction of trace amount of  $\mathrm{Ni^{2 + }}$  into the electrolyte (Figure 25b). $^{241}$  The  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  cell shows electrochemical stability window of over  $3.4\mathrm{V}$  and a discharge voltage of  $2.44\mathrm{V}$ . As a conclusion, tuning pH in the electrolyte can alter the redox reaction mechanism and improve energy density for developing practical ZIBs for GSES.

Further development of high-performance and cost-effective membranes shows promise to contribute to ZIBs for practical applications. The practical  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery can be achieved through scalable production from research laboratory to industry. As shown in Figure 25c, a prototype lab-scale membrane-free  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  flow battery with a capacity of  $1200\mathrm{mAh}$  has been fabricated and delivers a high specific

capacity with a long life of over 500 cycles.[242] Such a  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery is believed to able to meet the requirements of GSES after further improvement and optimization. In addition,  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  batteries with the cathode  $\mathrm{Mn^{2 + } / MnO_2}$  chemistry are feasible to greatly scale up by various cell designs such as pouch and prismatic cell packs, providing high flexibility to meet different requirements for practical GSES applications. As shown in Figure 25d, when two such single cells are connected in series, the output voltage of the electrolyte-decoupled  $\mathrm{Zn - MnO_2}$  battery is doubled, reaching  $\sim 5.44\mathrm{V}$  without sacrificing the capacity.[242] When two individual cells are connected in parallel, the aforementioned battery shows a capacity of  $\sim 6660$  mAh with similar discharge potential of  $\sim 2.7\mathrm{V}$ . The designed battery pack demonstrates practical energy storage capability.

Some researchers have concentrated on developing new Mn-based materials for high energy density ZIBs. For the Li-insertion cathodes, traditional  $\mathrm{AMn_2O_4}$  (A = Zn, Co, Ni) composite materials can improve the cycling stability as compared to the single materials.[243] Therefore, it is convenient to explore these materials for facilitating Zn-insertion in ZIBs. In this regard, Guo and co-workers have proven the efficacy of  $\mathrm{NiMn_2O_4}$  nanoparticles with a carbon matrix as the cathode for ZIBs, which exhibits a high rate capacity of  $98.5\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at 1200 mA g $^{-1}$  and outstanding cycling stability for 850 cycles.[244] The insertion of  $\mathrm{Zn^{2+}}$  into the structure of spinel  $\mathrm{ZnMn_2O_4}$  has also been verified.[245,246] In short, integrating functionalities of diverse metal oxides with  $\mathrm{MnO_2}$  provides pathways toward the development of efficient cathode materials for ZIBs.

3.6.2. V-Based Cathodes for ZIBs. The valence states of V undergo a transition from  $+2$  to  $+5$  during redox reactions of the electrochemical cell, proving the potential of V-based cathodes for achieving high capacity by means of multielectron reactions.[79] The mechanism of V-based cathodes governing

a

![](images/93648fbb9667981512ae8bdfb697462ff02d284dcf17dbf8f0a6b049d8db5404.jpg)  
e

![](images/fe23d99eef8a42109c4897f60c1da3e6af11a505f10972eaa1b7d3a20f71660a.jpg)

![](images/401a55f06edfb80265143ec4977fd3a541c713261996549776688a29c145abaf.jpg)  
d

![](images/104db72d3cd9439fd69f10eaad4e022936ca29e60062918878975ae0102d672b.jpg)

![](images/0ea242a1667a8837bf35d973894d45bb73c319e2eef71dd7f061f2a156ef1fce.jpg)

![](images/104b85beefb49497f98ffe1f9f77f127a705a265ea26c76d5e88f3e05bae6fbf.jpg)  
9  
Figure 26. Typical examples of  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8$  as cathode material for ZIBs. (a) Schematic of the rechargeable  $\mathrm{Zn - H_2V_3O_8}$  battery. (b) SEM image of the prepared  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8$  nanowires. (c) TEM and EDS mapping images in full discharge state of the  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8$  electrode after three cycles. (d) Charge/ discharge profiles at  $0.1\mathrm{A g}^{-1}$  of the initial three cycles and (e) cycle performance at  $5.0\mathrm{A g}^{-1}$  of  $\mathrm{Zn - H_2V_3O_8}$  battery. Reproduced with permission from ref 252. Copyright 2017 Wiley-VCH. (f) Rate capability at different rates and (g) long cycling stability at  $20\mathrm{C}$  of the  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8/$  graphene cathode. Reproduced with permission from ref 253. Copyright 2018 Wiley-VCH.

the  $\mathrm{Zn^{2 + }}$  insertion/extraction in the host structure is similar to the traditional LIBs.79 Recently, vanadium oxides,  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8$  and  $\mathrm{MV}_x\mathrm{O}_y$ $(\mathbf{M} = \mathbf{Li},\mathbf{Na},\mathbf{K},\mathbf{Z}\mathbf{n},$  etc.), have been investigated as novel V-based cathodes.224 The previously reported vanadium-based materials in ZIBs have mainly focused on layered vanadium oxides and have shown short cycle life and fast capacity fade.224 Until recent years, many advanced methods have been practiced to improve vanadium oxide materials for AZIBs. Huang and coworkers introduced a novel  $\mathrm{V}_{2}\mathrm{O}_{5}$  nanopaper as the cathode in ZIBs for enhancing their capacity and cycling stability.247 Similarly, Yang and co-workers have found that  $\mathrm{V}_{2}\mathrm{O}_{5}$  with structural  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  improves the  $\mathrm{Zn^{2 + }}$  intercalation and thus increases the energy density of ZIBs.248 Furthermore, Zhou and co-workers have introduced N in vanadium oxides with reversible cationic  $(\mathrm{V}^{3 + }$  to  $\mathrm{V}^{2 + })$  and anionic  $(\mathrm{N}^{3 - }$  to  $\mathrm{N}^{2 - })$  redox reactions for achieving a high rate capability of  $200\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at  $30\mathrm{A g^{-1}}$  and excellent cycling stability after 2000 cycles.249

In 2006, vanadium oxide hydrate  $\left(\mathrm{H}_{2} \mathrm{~V}_{3} \mathrm{O}_{8}\right)$ , comprised of  $\mathrm{VO}_{6}$  octahedrons together with  $\mathrm{VO}_{5}$  trigonal bipyramids by hydrogen bonds, has been reported as a promising cathode material for LIBs, which has an excellent  $\mathrm{Li}^{+}$ insertion capability.[250] In a similar fashion, attempts have been made to

realize the insertion of  $\mathrm{Zn^{2+}}$  into the layered structure of  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8$ . Compared to the weaker van der Waals force in the layered vanadium oxides such as  $\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5$ , the hydrogen bonds in  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8$  maintain structural integrity during charge/discharge processes and higher electronic conductivity.[251] For instance, Mai and co-workers employed a  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8$  nanowire cathode, zinc anode, and  $3m\mathrm{Zn}(\mathrm{CF}_3\mathrm{SO}_3)_2$  electrolyte to assemble a high-performance ZIB system, as illustrated in Figure 26a.[252] Figure 26b illustrates the SEM morphology of  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8$  nanowires with a uniform size of  $80 - 120~\mathrm{nm}$  which supports electronic conduction. In addition, Figure 26c shows the TEM-EDS patterns that confirm the intercalation of  $\mathrm{Zn^{2+}}$  into the  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8$ . When subjected to electrochemical cycling, the  $\mathrm{Zn - H_2V_3O_8}$  battery yields superior reversible capacity of  $\sim400\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  and a high current density of  $5\mathrm{A g^{-1}}$  with a capacity of  $113.9\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  (Figure 26d,e). The battery also delivers a high capacity retention of  $94.3\%$  after 1000 cycles at  $5\mathrm{A g^{-1}}$  as shown in Figure 26e. To contribute more active sites and larger specific capacity, Wang and co-workers harnessed the high conductivity of graphene networks by synthesizing a  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8$  nanowire/graphene composite material as the cathode for ZIBs.[253] The assembled battery exhibits a high rate capacity of  $270\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at

![](images/3a24e31ac5de59d5e490ee3edb1a507e53950d56599ce5961e65e321821b4d4e.jpg)

(a) Schematic of the  $\mathrm{Zn - Zn_{0.25}V_2O_5}$  nanobelt cell in an aqueous electrolyte of  $1\mathrm{M}\mathrm{ZnSO}_4$  in discharge state. (b) Scheme showing reversible water intercalation into  $\mathrm{Zn_{0.25}V_2O_5\cdot nH_2O}$  and water de-intercalation accompanying  $\mathrm{Zn^{2 + }}$  intercalation upon electrochemical discharge. The red and blue spheres represent O and H, respectively; the  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  molecules interact with the oxygen layers through hydrogen bonding. Here  $y > z > n$  , as a fraction of intercalated  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  remains in the discharged material. (c) Galvanostatic discharge and charge profiles of the  $\mathrm{Zn_{0.25}V_2O_5\cdot nH_2O}$  freestanding cathode at 1 C. (d) Galvanostatic discharge profiles at different rates  $(1\mathrm{C} = 300\mathrm{mA}\mathrm{g}^{-1})$  from 4 to  $20~\mathrm{C}$ . (e) Extended cycling performance and the corresponding CE at  $8\mathrm{C}$  (current density  $2400\mathrm{mA}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$ ), showing  $>80\%$  of the capacity retention (with respect to the highest capacity of  $260\mathrm{mAh}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$ ) after 1000 cycles. Reproduced with permission from ref 254. Copyright 2016 Springer Nature. (f) Rate capability and (g) long-term cycling performance at  $10\mathrm{A}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$  of  $\mathrm{Zn - Zn_{0.3}V_2O_5\cdot 1.5H_2O}$  NFs batteries. Reproduced with permission from ref 255. Copyright 2019 The American Association for the Advancement of Science.

![](images/73ac4481462da39f25e1781901521ea70ed1368be6773a1111b37b828ee9caac.jpg)

20 C and an excellent cycling stability of up to 2000 cycles with a capacity retention of  $87\%$ , as shown in Figure 26f,g. It is speculated that the introduction of graphene networks can further improve the performance of  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{V}_3\mathrm{O}_8$  nanowires as cathode for ZIBs.

Emerging as a new class of cathode materials, metal vanadium oxides,  $\mathrm{MV}_x\mathrm{O}_y$  ( $\mathrm{M} = \mathrm{Li}$ , Na, K, Zn, etc.), with or without structural water act as pillars to provide fast and reversible  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}$  intercalation/deintercalation during battery cycling.[224] Nazar and co-workers have reported nanobelts of vanadium oxide pillared by interlayer  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}$  and water ( $\mathrm{Zn}_{0.25}\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5\cdot n\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$ ) as a cathode for ZIB, as illustrated in Figure 27a.[254] Structurally, the  $\mathrm{Zn}_{0.25}\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5\cdot n\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  nanobelts consist of a double-sheet-type two-dimensional  $\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5$  framework (Figure 27b). The interlayer of the layered framework permits the insertion of water molecules from the electrolyte toward the cathode, thereby further

expanding the room for good  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}$  intercalation. Figure 27c,d illustrates the cycling results of the  $\mathrm{Zn}_{0.25}\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5\cdot n\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  cathode, showing a high capacity of  $282\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  in the initial cycle and fast discharge rate with capacities of 223 and  $183\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at 15 and  $20\mathrm{C}$ , respectively. As for the cycling performance, the  $\mathrm{Zn}-\mathrm{Zn}_{0.25}\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5\cdot n\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  nanobelt based ZIB delivers a capacity retention of more than  $80\%$  after 1000 cycles, as shown in Figure 27e. In addition, Zheng and co-workers have reported hierarchically porous  $\mathrm{Zn}_{0.3}\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5\cdot 1.5\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  NFs synthesized by coinsertion of  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}/\mathrm{H}^+$  into VOOH as a novel cathode for ZIB.[255] As shown in Figure 27f,g, the  $\mathrm{Zn}_{0.3}\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5\cdot 1.5\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  NFs exhibits a high discharge capacity of  $265.2\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at a current density of  $10\mathrm{A g^{-1}}$ , along with long cycling stability with  $96\%$  capacity retention at  $10\mathrm{A g^{-1}}$  after 20000 cycles.

Taking advantage of the smaller size of  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}$  (0.76 Å), as compared to  $\mathrm{Na}^{+}$  (0.99 Å), numerous researchers have studied

The inset picture represents the TEM image at a low magnification. (c) Crystal structure of  $\mathrm{Na}_2\mathrm{V}_6\mathrm{O}_{16}\cdot x\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$ . (d) Rate capacities at different current rates and (e) cycling capacity comparison at three different current rates of 15, 25, and  $40\mathrm{C}$  for 300, 500, and 1000 cycles, respectively, for the NVOH cathode. Reproduced with permission from ref 226. Copyright 2018 American Chemical Society. (f) SEM image of NVO nanowire. (g) Cycling performance of NVO at  $1.0\mathrm{A}\mathrm{g}^{-1}$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 220. Copyright 2018 Wiley-VCH.

![](images/b6c7aedafd8d0aa644911bbd0ac5a1792337ce3031c76815d139d1d11c90166f.jpg)

the insertion of  $\mathrm{Na^{+}}$  into the vanadium oxide layers for improving the electrochemical performance of ZIBs. For instance, Kim and co-workers prepared  $\mathrm{Na_2V_6O_{16}\cdot 3H_2O}$  (NVOH) nanorod powder via a rapid microwave technique. The intrinsic morphology is shown in Figure 28a.[226] The low-resolution inset image in Figure 28b clearly reflects the core-shell structure of NVOH, while the high-resolution image reveals distinguishable lattice fringes separated from a major portion of "fringe-free" domains. In addition, the crystal structure of  $\mathrm{Na_2V_6O_{16}\cdot xH_2O}$  with water molecules, as shown in Figure 28c, confirms the growth direction of nanorods along the  $a$ -axis. When cycled, the NVOH nanorods achieves a highly reversible capacity of  $113.95\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at a current rate of  $55.4\mathrm{C}$ , and excellent cycling stability with a capacity retention of over  $80\%$  after 1000 cycles (Figure 28d,e). Likewise, Mai and coworkers have reported a novel structural variant of  $\mathrm{Na_{0.33}V_2O_5}$  (NVO) nanowire, as shown in Figure 28f.[220] A ZIB based on the NVO nanowire exhibits reasonable cycling stability with a capacity retention over  $93\%$  for 1000 cycles compared with the NVOH nanorods (Figure 28g). Since  $\mathrm{K^{+}}$  and  $\mathrm{Ca^{2+}}$  are larger than  $\mathrm{Li^{+}}$  and  $\mathrm{Na^{+}}$ , they lead to excellent ion diffusion channels and stable crystal structure for ZIBs. This explains why

potassium vanadates, such as  $\mathrm{K}_2\mathrm{V}_8\mathrm{O}_{21}$  with its tunnel structure, show phenomenal  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}$  diffusion.[256] Wang and co-workers have further enhanced the electrochemical performance of potassium vanadates by combining defect engineering with carbon.[225] Besides the introduction of  $\mathrm{Zn}^{2+}$ ,  $\mathrm{Na}^+$ , and  $\mathrm{K}^+$ , other ions (such as  $\mathrm{Li}^+$  and  $\mathrm{Ca}^{2+}$ ) can also insert into vanadium oxides as ZIB cathodes to improve the performance.[257,258]

# 3.7. Magnesium-Ion Batteries

Magnesium-ion batteries (MgIBs) have been regarded as a promising candidate for GSES owing to their low cost, inherent safety (no dendrites), and high theoretical energy density.[259-261] Magnesium as a multivalent metal has a proven record of yielding a higher specific volumetric capacity of 3833 mAh cm $^{-3}$  than that of lithium metal (2046 mAh cm $^{-3}$ ).[259] Although Mg metal can be handled in ambient atmosphere for the preparation of electrodes, the growth of passivating surface films in electrolyte and the difficulty of intercalating Mg $^{2+}$  into cathode materials inhibit the electrochemical reactions.[261] Previously, Levi and co-workers achieved a significant breakthrough in the development of rechargeable MgIBs for potential application.[262] To explain, a MgIB has been introduced that is comprised of  $\mathrm{Mg}_x\mathrm{Mo}_3\mathrm{S}_4$  cathode, Mg metal anode, and an

![](images/1d428a5951302a6f90adb7abdb91bb0fd3d1382976e99e44fe8ec1e0015eb8cb.jpg)  
a

![](images/853b973ab3f3bf187a4e567753910666d71c7f9b5329a386ff4a1803ab8c44f8.jpg)  
C

![](images/5d6dec70e9a33b1e8c7815a0069c32bbe92d78372cc678aac5fbb2fefd08ca64.jpg)

![](images/8488fee10a10f955e479f452fe856e4938d240a7877ffdd56182c0e9b517f2e7.jpg)  
Figure 29. Typical examples of alloy materials as anodes for MgIBs. (a) Schematic illustration of deinsertion/insertion of  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$  in  $\mathrm{Mg}_3\mathrm{Bi}_2$  alloy particles, their crystal structures, and high-resolution TEM images. (b) Galvanostatic discharge/charge voltage profiles and (c) cycling performance at  $0.2\mathrm{A g^{-1}}$  of PBA-  $\mathrm{Mg}_3\mathrm{Bi}_2$  full cell with  $1\mathrm{M}$  LiTFSI-  $2\mathrm{M}$ $\mathrm{Mg(TFSI)}_2 / \mathrm{AN}$  electrolyte. Reproduced with permission from ref 265. Copyright 2018 American Chemical Society. (d) Cycling performance of the porous  $\mathrm{Bi}_3\mathrm{Sn}_2$  anode at  $1000\mathrm{mA g^{-1}}$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 268. Copyright 2019 Royal Society of Chemistry.

electrolyte solution of  $\mathrm{Mg(AlCl_2BuEt)_2}$  in tetrahydrofuran. The  $\mathrm{Mg}_x\mathrm{Mo}_3\mathrm{S}_4$  cathode is responsible for aiding the reversible intercalation of  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$ , hence achieving the fast reaction kinetics. However, the energy density and operating voltage of the MgIB need further improvement. In addition, the passivating layer of  $\mathrm{Mg}$  metal in traditional organic solutions prevents the reaction of  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$ . Therefore, studies for developing improved anode materials and  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$  intercalation cathodes in suitable electrolytes are needed for the future MgIBs in GSES applications.

3.7.1. Anode Materials for MgIBs. The number of studies on MgIB anode materials is much less than those on cathodes due to the limitation of an insulating SEI layer on the surface of Mg metal anodes.[261] To solve this problem, electrolytes such as Grignard reagents have been proven effective for enabling reversible plating/stripping of  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$  at the Mg metal anode.[262] However, these electrolytes are usually difficult to synthesize and are sometimes corrosive with typical current collectors.[265] Therefore, the alloy-type anode materials have recently attracted much attention in MgIBs.[266,267] A major downside concerning alloy-type anode materials (such as Ge, Si, and P) is their

![](images/2cb959d0a122aab295e363cdc8c15e0c832e061e0aecdfaec86592123b98574a.jpg)

![](images/786616a2bc23776dcf84428cf0f0e9df6fea3bcb6d5187bd4c0bb993321750ac.jpg)

![](images/245829b15cc4f50963997ea08dd4a348f0e0bd66ab1d1ef7353c1db0f24f3892.jpg)  
Figure 30. Typical examples of magnesium vanadium oxides as cathode materials for MgIBs. (a) Schematic diagrams of the formation of the bilayer-structured  $\mathrm{Mg_{0.3}V_2O_5\cdot 1.1H_2O}$ . (b) Charge/discharge curves and (c) cycling performances of  $\mathrm{Mg_{0.3}V_2O_5\cdot 1.1H_2O}$ ,  $\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5\cdot n\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$ , and  $\mathrm{Mg_{0.3}V_2O_5}$ . (d) Schematic illustration and (e) charge/discharge profiles at different cycles (1st, 2nd, 10th, 50th, and 100th) of full cell with  $\mathrm{Mg_{0.3}V_2O_5\cdot 1.1H_2O}$  cathode,  $\mathrm{Mg(TFSI)_2 - ACN}$  electrolyte, and  $\mathrm{MgNaTi_3O_7}$  anode. Reproduced with permission from ref 269. Copyright 2019 Elsevier.

![](images/a1373f35314d9648e6c446dedc5a939ed24902d21b78393c28c4cc62ce203ff5.jpg)

difficulty to undergo Mg insertion due to their sluggish diffusion kinetics and large volume expansion during cycles.[268] Hitherto, some reports about alloy anodes have mainly concentrated on Bi and Sn metal materials, but the pristine Bi and Sn metal materials are insufficient to meet the demand of MgIBs for energy applications.[266] Therefore, the development of the anodes still requires substantial improvements and structural optimization. Yao and co-workers have synthesized a nanoclustered  $\mathrm{Mg}_3\mathrm{Bi}_2$  alloy as MgIB anode in noncorrosive electrolytes.[265] The assynthesized alloy shows high reversibility for  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$  deinsertion/insertion, as shown in Figure 29a. Furthermore, the MgIB based on PBA cathode and  $\mathrm{Mg}_3\mathrm{Bi}_2$  alloy anode achieves a high discharge voltage of  $\sim 2\mathrm{V}$  and long cycling stability after 200 cycles (Figure 29b,c). Similarly, Zhang and co-workers have investigated a porous Bi-Sn alloy, which exhibits excellent capacity retention of over  $93\%$  for 200 cycles, as shown in Figure 29d.[268]

3.7.2. Cathode Materials for MgIBs. Unlike insertion of  $\mathrm{Li^{+}}$  and  $\mathrm{Na^{+}}$ , it is much more challenging to insert  $\mathrm{Mg^{2 + }}$  into the host materials primarily due to the strong interaction between the host lattice and  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2 + }$ . Many materials have been reported as cathodes for MgIBs, including PBAs,[265] vanadium oxides,[269] transition-metal sulfides,[270] and polyanionic compounds.[271] Among them, vanadium oxide cathodes have gained relatively more attention for delivering good cycling stability in MgIBs.

The stronger interactions between  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$  and oxide host lattices are responsible for slow  $\mathrm{Mg}$  diffusion.[261] Therefore, further developments have been made in synthesizing nanomaterials (such as  $\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5$  aerogels or nanowires) as cathode materials for decreasing the diffusion distance of  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$ .[272,273] Another strategy to ensure the insertion of  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$  is to alter the layered structure of vanadium oxides for  $\mathrm{MgIB}$  cathodes. Concerning this, Jacobson and co-workers put forward the idea of introducing Mo to vanadium oxide layers for processing a microporous molybdenum-vanadium oxide molecular sieve  $\mathrm{Mo}_{2.5+y}\mathrm{VO}_{9+\delta}$  as a cathode for  $\mathrm{MgIBs}$ .[273] The crystal structure of  $\mathrm{Mo}_{2.5+y}\mathrm{VO}_{9+\delta}$  is useful in providing diffusion pathways for small guest molecules and thereby enhancing  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$  intercalation. The electrochemical testing of  $\mathrm{Mo}_{2.5+y}\mathrm{VO}_{9+\delta}$  cathode provides a high capacity of  $397\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  along with plausible intercalation up to 3.49 of  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$  ions per formula unit. Similarly, Mai and coworkers have reported  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$  and water molecule co-intercalated vanadium oxide ( $\mathrm{Mg}_{0.3}\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5\cdot 1.1\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$ ) as a  $\mathrm{MgIB}$  cathode (Figure 30a), showing higher capacity and longer cycling stability than the pristine  $\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5\cdot n\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  and waterless  $\mathrm{Mg}_{0.3}\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5$ , as shown in Figure 30b,c.[269] When a  $\mathrm{MgIB}$  is assembled with  $\mathrm{Mg}_{0.3}\mathrm{V}_2\mathrm{O}_5\cdot 1.1\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  cathode,  $\mathrm{Mg(TFSI)}_2$ -ACN electrolyte, and  $\mathrm{MgNaTi}_3\mathrm{O}_7$  anode, it delivers a high average voltage of  $1.5\mathrm{V}$  and a good capacity retention of  $42\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  after 100 cycles

![](images/082a28517d7135ca037cbe984eff68169b986a0307b18413b078f3dbbf587fd5.jpg)  
a

![](images/fab6434a7a35672d81d0774c76fb0ca9d48ae09564b59754bd9dc749f1571ca2.jpg)
