These features thus provide a new outlook to develop more efficient electrocatalysts for achieving longer cycles and more cost-effective electrochemical systems than the traditional

HGBs. In addition, the low-cost  $\mathrm{Ni - H_2}$  batteries have been recently implemented by a California startup named EnerVenue. This has substantially accelerated the development of safe, maintenance-free, and cost-efficient clean energy storage batteries for LSES applications.

9.2.3.  $\mathsf{Mn - H_2}$  Battery. In order to further decrease the cost of the HGBs, a  $\mathrm{MnO}_2\mathrm{-H}_2$  battery system based on a low-priced solid  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  cathode and  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas anode in alkaline electrolyte has been proposed.[739] The  $\mathrm{MnO}_2\mathrm{-H}_2$  cell operates at a voltage of  $0.7\mathrm{V}$  and achieves over 25000 low earth orbit cycles with energy density of 32.6 Wh kg $^{-1}$ , which is slightly higher than the traditional Ni-H $_2$  battery.[739] However, the energy density of this HGB has been insufficient to cater to LSES demands. Therefore, a new electrochemical  $\mathrm{MnO}_2\mathrm{-H}_2$  battery system for the cathode has been further reported by Cui and co-workers, which is based on the deposition and stripping chemistry between soluble  $\mathrm{Mn}^{2+}$  and solid  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  in acidic electrolytes. The two-electron-transfer reaction of the  $\mathrm{Mn}^{2+}/\mathrm{MnO}_2$  cathode with a theoretical capacity of  $\sim616\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  is fundamentally different from the traditional solid-solid transformation in alkaline and neutral electrolytes. This in turn is responsible for the enhancement of the cell capacity and material utilization.[709] The redox reactions of the new  $\mathrm{Mn - H_2}$  battery with the cathode  $\mathrm{Mn}^{2+}/\mathrm{MnO}_2$  chemistry can be described in the following:

Cathode:

$$
\begin{array}{l} \mathrm {M n O} _ {2} + 4 \mathrm {H} ^ {+} + 2 \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \leftrightarrow \mathrm {M n} ^ {2 +} + 2 \mathrm {H} _ {2} \mathrm {O} \\ E ^ {\circ} = 1. 2 3 \mathrm {V} \tag {54} \\ \end{array}
$$

Anode:

$$
2 \mathrm {H} ^ {+} + 2 \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \leftrightarrow \mathrm {H} _ {2} \quad E ^ {\circ} = 0 \mathrm {V} \tag {55}
$$

Overall:

$$
\begin{array}{l} \mathrm {M n O} _ {2} + 2 \mathrm {H} ^ {+} + \mathrm {H} _ {2} \leftrightarrow \mathrm {M n} ^ {2 +} + 2 \mathrm {H} _ {2} \mathrm {O} \\ E ^ {\circ} = 1. 2 3 \mathrm {V} \tag {56} \\ \end{array}
$$

Figure 89a shows the working principle of the new  $\mathrm{Mn - H_2}$  battery with the cathode  $\mathrm{Mn^{2 + } / MnO_2}$  chemistry during charge/ discharge states. It can be seen that the battery adopts a cathodeless permeable CF, a glass fiber membrane as the separator, a Pt/ C catalyst coated on CF as the  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  anode, and a soluble  $\mathrm{MnSO_4}$  aqueous solution as the electrolyte. During charging, the soluble  $\mathrm{Mn}^{2 + }$  transforms into solid  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  on the cathode, while HER is driven by the highly active Pt/C catalyst on the anode. Conversely, during discharge, the deposited solid  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  on the cathode is dissolved back to soluble  $\mathrm{Mn}^{2 + }$  into the electrolyte and  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  is oxidized on the anode. The reversibility of the  $\mathrm{Mn}^{2 + }/$ $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  reactions can be further demonstrated by SEM images along with their corresponding EDX spectra, as shown in Figure 89b-d. It is evident in Figure 89b that the pristine CF has a smooth surface with high purity. After charging, however, a nanoscale  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  appears on the CF, showing the formation of solid  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  (Figure 89c). After the first full discharge to  $0.5\mathrm{V}$ , the solid  $\mathrm{MnO}_2$  on the cathode nearly disappears and returns to the original state (Figure 89d). Consequently, the reversible reaction of the  $\mathrm{Mn}^{2 + }/\mathrm{MnO}_2$  for the cathode and the conversion of  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas provide ultrafast and stable battery operational dynamics. As shown in Figure 89e, the discharge curves show a discharge voltage plateau of about  $1.25\mathrm{V}$  with a CE of  $100\%$  at a current density of  $10\mathrm{mAcm^{-2}}$ . When the discharge current density increased from  $10\mathrm{mAcm^{-2}}$  to  $100\mathrm{mAcm^{-2}}$  (discharge time of  $36~s$ ), the discharge curve experienced a slight decline

while the capacity was still maintained at nearly  $1\mathrm{mAhcm}^{-2}$ , hence exhibiting a remarkably high power density (Figure 89f). In addition, it was demonstrated that two such Swagelok-type  $\mathrm{Mn - H_2}$  cells (Figure 89g) connected in series were capable of lighting a blue LED for a few hours when charged for only  $3\mathrm{min}$ . Moreover, the battery system showed nearly no capacity decay over 10000 cycles due to the high reversibility of the cathode  $\mathrm{Mn^{2 + } / MnO_{2}}$  and anode HER/HOR reactions, as shown in Figure 89h. In spite of the high power density and long cycling stability, the  $\mathrm{Mn - H_2}$  cells still have capacity limitations in meeting the needs of LSES applications. In order to increase the cell capacity, a cylindrical cell assembly was proposed by Cui and co-workers, as shown in Figure 89i, which exhibits a higher discharge capacity of  $\sim 14\mathrm{mAh}$  along with a cycling stability for 1400 cycles, strengthening feasibility of  $\mathrm{Mn - H_2}$  cells for LSES (Figure 89j). Since the cell capacity largely depends on the surface area of the cathode CF, it is critical for future work to focus on developing low cost substrate materials having high  $\mathrm{MnO_2}$  deposition capacity for practical applications.

9.2.4. Lithium Intercalation Compound- $\mathsf{H}_2$  Battery. Originally developed by Sony in the early 1990s, LIBs have offered remarkable prospects as alternative energy storage systems and have been successfully applied in portable electronics and EVs.[80] The rapidly growing commercial applications for LIBs are mainly because of the stable  $\mathsf{Li}^+$ extraction/intercalation on anode and cathode, explaining why they offer brighter prospects in LSES applications. A large amount of the cathode materials in LIBs have attracted significant interest in related applications.[740-742] Recently, Chen and co-workers have studied a new HGB based on spinel LMO cathode and  $\mathsf{H}_2$  anode, namely,  $\mathrm{LMO - H_2}$ , exhibiting better rate performance and cycling stability than that of traditional aqueous LIBs based on the LMO cathode.[718] As shown in Figure 90a, the  $\mathrm{LMO - H_2}$  battery adopts the commercial Pt/C loaded with GDL as hydrogen gas anode and the LMO as cathode. The energy conversions for the  $\mathrm{LMO - H_2}$  batteries are carried out by means of extraction/insertion of  $\mathsf{Li}^+$ on the cathode and HER/HOR on the anode through the following electrode reactions:

Cathode:

$$
\mathrm {L i M n} _ {2} \mathrm {O} _ {4} \leftrightarrow \mathrm {L i} _ {0. 5} \mathrm {M n} _ {2} \mathrm {O} _ {4} + 0. 5 \mathrm {L i} ^ {+} + 0. 5 \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \tag {57}
$$

Anode:

$$
2 \mathrm {H} _ {2} \mathrm {O} + 2 \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \leftrightarrow 2 \mathrm {O H} ^ {-} + \mathrm {H} _ {2} \tag {58}
$$

Overall:

$$
\begin{array}{l} 4 \mathrm {L i M n} _ {2} \mathrm {O} _ {4} + 2 \mathrm {H} _ {2} \mathrm {O} \leftrightarrow 4 \mathrm {L i} _ {0. 5} \mathrm {M n} _ {2} \mathrm {O} _ {4} + 2 \mathrm {L i} ^ {+} + 2 \mathrm {O H} ^ {-} \\ + \mathrm {H} _ {2} \tag {59} \\ \end{array}
$$

Figure 90b,c show the characteristic morphology of the commercial LMO powder with particle size of  $\sim 250\mathrm{nm}$ . For the Pt/C catalyst, several nanometers of Pt particles are located on the surface of carbon as shown in Figure 90d,e. The LMO- $\mathrm{H}_2$  cell exhibits a high discharge voltage plateau of  $\sim 1.3\mathrm{V}$  (Figure 90f) and a superior rate of  $50\mathrm{C}$ , which demonstrates an effective compatibility between the  $\mathrm{Li^{+}}$  cathode and the  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  anode, as well as the fast reaction kinetics of the  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas anode (Figure 90g). In addition, the LMO- $\mathrm{H}_2$  cell shows stable cycling performance with capacity retention up to  $\sim 80\%$  of the initial capacity after 600 cycles (Figure 90h). The cyclic performance is believed to improve by enhancing the structural stability of the cathode

![](images/1ce16184dca68a3025f78ea068a095904d4b107a4d728da1f6122a620963c13f.jpg)

![](images/7cd72a7a6d22ca5e573cf66a58e3d0ac3e53c9dd725af281fc87fdcbb824bbc1.jpg)

![](images/f2ef79dbdc52cba7da7551b2ae24023215579a1c94476913080494bcb543c50b.jpg)

![](images/534a4262f6d7dc74d2ac74b674e6a00d8f35b07e08eafd19df3e6bdc1132ad05.jpg)  
Figure 91. LCO–H $_2$  and LFP–H $_2$  batteries based on LCO and LFP cathode materials. (a) Charge/discharge curves of the LCO–H $_2$  battery at different discharge rates. (b) Cycling performance of the LCO–H $_2$  and recycled LCO–H $_2$  batteries at 2 C. (c) SEM image of the LCO electrode after 50 cycles in the LCO–H $_2$  battery. (d) Charge/discharge curves of the LFP–H $_2$  battery at different discharge rates. (e) Cycling performance of the LFP–H $_2$  and recycled LFP–H $_2$  batteries at 10 C. (f) SEM image of the LFP electrode after 50 cycles in the LFP–H $_2$  battery. Reproduced with permission from ref 719. Copyright 2021. Editorial office of Chem. J. Chinese Universities.

![](images/c65449fc3b5e62bc224fddc24ac34346133c6e65d49d2f0d288aff21638b6e30.jpg)

![](images/57194af704004d260a19531f8c01268623993f74d5ef05d9814f9f6980d3ebb9.jpg)

materials in optimized electrolytes. Therefore, there is an emerging trend toward the exploration of new HGB systems based on the  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas anode as alternatives to fulfill the increasing demands of LSES.

In addition to LMO, other Li intercalation compounds such as LCO and LFP have capabilities to serve as excellent cathode materials for HGBs. Chen and co-workers developed other lithium intercalation compound- $\mathrm{H}_2$  gas batteries, such as  $\mathrm{LCO}-\mathrm{H}_2$  and  $\mathrm{LFP}-\mathrm{H}_2$  batteries, which are based on  $\mathrm{Pt/C}$ -based  $\mathrm{H}_2$  anode and LCO or LFP cathodes in mild aqueous electrolytes. The working mechanisms of such batteries are similar to that of the  $\mathrm{LMO}-\mathrm{H}_2$  battery.[719] It is evident from Figure 91a that the  $\mathrm{LCO}-\mathrm{H}_2$  battery exhibits a high discharge voltage plateau of  $1.22\mathrm{V}$  at  $1\mathrm{C}$  and retains around  $1.08\mathrm{V}$  with a discharge capacity of  $49\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  at a high discharge rate of  $10\mathrm{C}$ . On the other hand, the battery shows capacity decay after 50 cycles (Figure 91b), which is ascribed to the instability of the LCO in aqueous electrolytes, as demonstrated in Figure 91c. To prolong the cycling lifetime of the  $\mathrm{LCO}-\mathrm{H}_2$  battery, a new LCO cathode was employed with the same  $\mathrm{Pt/C}$ -based  $\mathrm{H}_2$  anode to form a recycled  $\mathrm{LCO}-\mathrm{H}_2$  battery. Such an electrochemical system is capable of delivering comparable charge/discharge capacities and cycling stability as those of the pristine  $\mathrm{LCO}-\mathrm{H}_2$  battery, demonstrating the robustness of the  $\mathrm{H}_2$  gas anode for rechargeable HGBs. Similarly, the  $\mathrm{LFP}-\mathrm{H}_2$  battery also demonstrates high discharge capacities of  $83\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$  at  $0.5\mathrm{C}$  and exceptional rate of  $10\mathrm{C}$ , as shown in Figure 91d. In this case, the cycled LFP cathode has been replaced by a new one and continuously tested for evaluating the cycling performance of the recycled  $\mathrm{LFP}-\mathrm{H}_2$  battery. Although the  $\mathrm{LFP}-\mathrm{H}_2$  battery shows capacity decline at  $10\mathrm{C}$  after 50 cycles, the recycled

$\mathrm{LFP}-\mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery can still reach the initial capacity level and cycling performance (Figure 91e) as compared to the pristine  $\mathrm{LFP}-\mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery. Such cycling instability is attributed to the unstable LFP electrode in aqueous solution rather than  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas electrode, as shown in the SEM micrograph in Figure 91f.

9.2.5. Prussian Blue Analogue- $\mathsf{H}_2$  Battery. PBAs, also known as metal hexacyanoferrate, have the advantages of open structures, multiple active sites, and environmental benignity.[209-211,743-751] Therefore, PBAs have attracted increasing attention as universal electrodes of aqueous batteries for various ion storage, such as metal ions  $(\mathrm{Li}^{+},\mathrm{Na}^{+}$ and  $\mathrm{K}^+$  ) and nonmetal ions  $(\mathrm{H}^{+}$ and  $\mathrm{NH_4^+})$  .[752,718] Considering the excellent properties of the  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  anode, Chen and co-workers proposed a category of aqueous PBA-H $_2$  batteries for GSES applications by rational combinations of PBAs as cathodes with the  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  anode for different cations  $(\mathrm{Na}^{+},\mathrm{K}^{+}$ and  $\mathrm{H}^{+}$  storage, referred to as PBA  $(\mathrm{Na}^{+}) - \mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery, PBA  $(\mathrm{K}^{+}) - \mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery, and PBA  $(\mathrm{H}^{+})-$ $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery, respectively.[753,754] Figure 92a schematically illustrates the working mechanism of the PBA-H $_2$  batteries based on different cations in aqueous electrolytes. During charge, cations  $(\mathrm{Na}^{+},\mathrm{K}^{+}$  or  $\mathrm{H}^{+}$ ) are removed from PBA cathode and  $\mathrm{H}^{+}$  cations move onto the GDL anode to form  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas. Conversely, during discharge, cations  $(\mathrm{Na}^{+},\mathrm{K}^{+}$  or  $\mathrm{H}^{+}$ ) insert into the PBA cathode and  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas is oxidized on the anode. The charge and discharge reactions of the PBA-H $_2$  batteries are expressed in the following equations:

Cathode:

$$
\mathrm {P B A} + x \mathrm {C} ^ {+} + x \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \leftrightarrow \mathrm {P B A} - x \mathrm {C} \tag {60}
$$

![](images/e15746754c179378002d55e317babeb3a7302238da1867dadaa4c0ad31f2cfb6.jpg)

![](images/b30f485d6788b6f0c904a70900d9d5970944c8252d1ea6efcb06a9338d2cd8d9.jpg)

![](images/f8e5c4727cf08eee8243693b025c87417bdff6b389ee5d15ac9d2d329f8b09c4.jpg)

![](images/95856be362f86583af349576da7b71f7e13114ddab277164104aed54897eb564.jpg)

![](images/eacbe88da2e6068499b0a259f021fdd319f92926f3c7f83c291f07cb7e717f53.jpg)

![](images/c2e6aec0750e59011ac65a9aa0f9432f80f5455f585b0e0fd002f1ce731895e2.jpg)

![](images/a75af5ada143b78e2e80f1b8e2c86e213eeb63b48b718cb6199de38731122591.jpg)  
Figure 92.  $\mathrm{PBA - H_2}$  batteries based on PBA cathode materials. (a) Working principle of  $\mathrm{PBA - H_2}$  battery accompanied by  $\mathrm{C}^+$  ( $\mathrm{C = Na, K, or H}$ ) ionic reactions at the cathode during charge and discharge. (b) Charge/discharge profiles of  $\mathrm{PBA(Na^{+}) - H_{2}}$  battery at various current rates ( $1\mathrm{C} = 50\mathrm{mAh}$ ,  $\mathbf{g}^{-1}$ ). (c) Charge/discharge profiles of  $\mathrm{PBA(K^{+}) - H_{2}}$  battery at various current rates. Reproduced with permission from ref 753. Copyright 2021 Elsevier. (d) Charge/discharge profiles of  $\mathrm{PBA(H^{+}) - H_{2}}$  battery at various current rates. (e) Rate performance comparison in electrolytes with different cations as the charge carriers. (f) Cycling performance of  $\mathrm{PBA(H^{+}) - H_{2}}$  battery at a current rate of  $960\mathrm{C}$  for 0.35 million cycles. (g) DSC test curves of different concentrations of  $\mathrm{H}_3\mathrm{PO}_4$  electrolyte from  $-93$  to  $20^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$  at a heating rate of  $5^{\circ}\mathrm{C}\min^{-1}$ . (h) Temperature-dependent ionic conductivity of different concentrations of  $\mathrm{H}_3\mathrm{PO}_4$  electrolytes. (i) Charge/discharge profiles of  $\mathrm{PBA(H^{+}) - H_{2}}$  battery under different temperatures. Reproduced with permission from ref 754. Copyright 2021 American Chemical Society.

![](images/4755cc975b4058516fd27d4a72b291d20dbdbbf0f7189046b897242ed96c9dcb.jpg)

![](images/c69033ab6c460d1890d93191d4ee4f759838e3e27c0e8c0a91c57d3028ea7429.jpg)

Anode:

$$
\mathrm {H} _ {2} \leftrightarrow 2 \mathrm {H} ^ {+} + 2 \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \tag {61}
$$

Overall:

$$
2 \mathrm {P B A} + \mathrm {H} _ {2} + 2 \mathrm {C} ^ {+} \leftrightarrow 2 \mathrm {P B A} - \mathrm {C} + 2 \mathrm {H} ^ {+},
$$

$$
x = 1 \text {a n d} C = N a, K, \text {o r} H \tag {62}
$$

As shown in Figure 92b, the  $\mathrm{PBA}(\mathrm{Na}^{+}) - \mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery shows outstanding rate performance, where the discharge capacities reach  $\sim 52$ , 47, 41, 34, and  $30\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at current rates of 5, 10, 20, 40, and  $60~\mathrm{C}$ , respectively. Even at a high rate of  $100\mathrm{C}$ , the battery capacity is still  $26\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$ . As shown in Figure 92c, the  $\mathrm{PBA}(\mathrm{K}^{+}) - \mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery delivers a discharge capacity of  $53\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  with a voltage plateau of  $\sim 1.09\mathrm{V}$  at a current rate of  $2\mathrm{C}$ . The charge/discharge curves of different current rates show a high capacity of  $47\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at  $5\mathrm{C}$  and the capacity remains at 20  $\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at a high rate of  $100\mathrm{C}$  (Figure 92c). In addition, the charge/discharge curves of the  $\mathrm{PBA}(\mathrm{H}^{+}) - \mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery performed at  $10\mathrm{C}$ ,  $80\mathrm{C}$ ,  $160\mathrm{C}$ ,  $320\mathrm{C}$ ,  $640\mathrm{C}$ , and  $960\mathrm{C}$  show capacities of

52, 48.3, 46.4, 43.8, 39.7, and  $35.9\mathrm{mAhg}^{-1}$ , which correspond to capacity retention of  $100\%$ ,  $93\%$ ,  $89\%$ ,  $84\%$ ,  $76\%$ , and  $69\%$  of the cell capacity at the rate of  $10\mathrm{C}$ , respectively (Figure 92d). As expected, the battery with  $\mathrm{K}^+$  or  $\mathrm{Na}^+$  metallic cations as charge carriers delivers inferior rate capacities as compared to that of  $\mathrm{PBA(H^{+}) - H_{2}}$  battery (Figure 92e), highlighting the ultrafast properties of  $\mathrm{PBA(H^{+}) - H_{2}}$  battery. Impressively, the PBA- $(\mathrm{H}^{+})-\mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery delivers a long-term stability of over 50000 cycles with initial capacity retention of  $90\%$  (Figure 92f). Meanwhile, it demonstrates cycle stability for over 0.35 million cycles at  $960\mathrm{C}$  and still retains over  $62\%$  of its original capacity and high CE of  $\sim 99.8\%$  (Figure 92f), exhibiting long-duration stable and reversible cyclability performance.

In addition to the ultrahigh rates, the  $\mathrm{PBA(H^{+}) - H_{2}}$  battery can also work well at ultralow-temperature conditions. A key challenge for low-temperature battery design is the electrolytes with high ionic conductivities. The physical state and ionic conductivity of the electrolytes  $(\mathrm{H}_3\mathrm{PO}_4)$  were tested at a series of low temperatures. To demonstrate the design of concentrated  $\mathrm{H}_3\mathrm{PO}_4$  electrolyte, the temperatures of the solid-liquid

![](images/5f0c57f7c9d93e01bebea3f21c9b01af352b9c485e673806fed64127bd87f29e.jpg)

![](images/1f2cfcf28652d9ea02fff7a2b2365ec3d384db05179af253fcaee53eb48df90d.jpg)

![](images/66b7a2b9569565009b1382b7fc2d4e1a6aa14fdb7c023e727a73ffb3894bc748.jpg)

![](images/caa3744898901e818185804bb6e13951ec29a640ddf9e12de5bce3cb70e30490.jpg)  
Figure 93.  $\mathrm{Fe - H_2}$  battery based on  $[\mathrm{Fe}(\mathrm{CN})_6]^{3 - } / [\mathrm{Fe}(\mathrm{CN})_6]^{4 - }$  redox couple cathode materials. (a) Working principle of  $\mathrm{Fe - H_2}$  battery in the charge and discharge processes. (b) Charge/discharge profiles at various current rates. (c) CE, EE, and capacity retention as a function of current. (d) Cycling performance at the charge/discharge current of  $20\mathrm{mA}$  with a charge capacity of  $0.3\mathrm{mAh}$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 721. Copyright 2020 Elsevier.

transitions of different concentrations of  $\mathrm{H}_3\mathrm{PO}_4$  electrolytes were explored by differential scanning calorimeter (DSC), as shown in Figure 92g. It was found that the heating process contained a solid-liquid phase transition temperature above  $-15^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$  at low-concentrations of  $\mathrm{H}_3\mathrm{PO}_4$ $(0 - 5\mathrm{M})$ . When the concentration of  $\mathrm{H}_3\mathrm{PO}_4$  electrolyte further increased to  $9\mathrm{M}$ , the freezing point tended to stabilize  $(< -80^{\circ}\mathrm{C})$ . As shown in Figure 92h, the ionic conductivity reached a maximal value when the electrolyte concentration was  $9\mathrm{M}$ . The ionic conductivity of  $9\mathrm{M}$ $\mathrm{H}_3\mathrm{PO}_4$  electrolyte was measured to be  $2.49\mathrm{mScm}^{-1}$  at  $-60^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ . As for the low-temperature performance, Chen and coworkers investigated the electrochemical behavior of the

$\mathrm{PBA(H^{+}) - H_{2}}$  battery with  $9\mathrm{M}$ $\mathrm{H}_3\mathrm{PO}_4$  electrolyte at various low temperatures. When the temperature decreased to  $-20^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ ,  $-40^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , and  $-60^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , the battery exhibited capacities of 47, 42, and  $30\mathrm{mAhg^{-1}}$  at  $5\mathrm{C}$ , respectively (Figure 92i). When the temperature further decreased to  $-80^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , which is close to the freezing point of electrolyte, the  $\mathrm{PBA(H^{+}) - H_{2}}$  battery could still provide  $54\%$  of its room-temperature capacity at  $0.5\mathrm{C}$ .

9.2.6.  $\mathsf{Fe - H_2}$  Battery. Due to the relatively sluggish redox reactions involving solid cathodes, the corresponding HGBs  $(\mathrm{Ni - H}_2,\mathrm{LMO - H}_2,$  and  $\mathrm{PBA - H_2})$  show limited rate capability, which is why it is preferred to apply liquid cathodes with high reversibility and fast kinetics. These two attributes have been

![](images/9af0f1410ffe08b5025e38827944d39ecb122f1b4e441a07821d246f09140782.jpg)

![](images/236473bfc61aed63d4d2431203a6256e12cdd04abe307ccc938bd00e5d1cd266.jpg)

![](images/446e8edd074e353e3d3ea4b4bdf627fe1a5836f98b6fe0e214a739567f707eaf.jpg)  
Figure 94. Working principles and electrochemical performance of some other HGBs. (a) Schematic illustration of  $\mathrm{Br}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  RFB. (b) Discharge curves at various current densities of the  $\mathrm{Br}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  RFB and digital photographs of flow solution before and after  $0.93\mathrm{h}$  of discharge at  $1\mathrm{C}$  ( $1\mathrm{C} = 0.9\mathrm{Acm}^{-2}$ ). Reproduced with permission from ref 762. Copyright 2012 The Electrochemical Society. (c) Schematic illustration of a hydrogen-storing quinone- $\mathrm{H}_2$  battery. (d) Long cycling stability of the quinone- $\mathrm{H}_2$  battery at  $10\mathrm{mA cm}^{-2}$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 720. Copyright 2018 American Chemical Society.

![](images/b537ec510708f5d59bd0a5cd7abb741cc4cdb8bbe2e7b61e75a83e1a4f124c84.jpg)

achieved by the low-cost  $\left[\mathrm{Fe}(\mathrm{CN})_{6}\right]^{3-}/\left[\mathrm{Fe}(\mathrm{CN})_{6}\right]^{4-}$  liquid redox molecules, which have attracted considerable attention in RFBs. $^{523,755}$  Therefore, Chen and co-workers have reported an Fe based HGB employing a  $\left[\mathrm{Fe}(\mathrm{CN})_{6}\right]^{3-}/\left[\mathrm{Fe}(\mathrm{CN})_{6}\right]^{4-}$  redox couple cathode and a hydrogen gas anode in alkaline solution, namely, an  $\mathrm{Fe}-\mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery. $^{721}$  Unlike RFBs that are driven by the flow of electrolytes through external pumping equipment, the  $\mathrm{Fe}-\mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery is designed as a static cell without using electrolyte pumping or a circulation system, which greatly eases the battery fabrication process and hence reduces the manufacturing cost. Figure 93a shows the working principle of the proposed aqueous  $\mathrm{Fe}-\mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery, where the  $\mathrm{H}_{2}\mathrm{O}/\mathrm{H}_{2}$  redox couple serves as the anode while the  $\left[\mathrm{Fe}(\mathrm{CN})_{6}\right]^{3-}/\left[\mathrm{Fe}(\mathrm{CN})_{6}\right]^{4-}$  redox couple serves as the cathode, whose reactions can be described in the following equations:

Cathode:

$$
\left[ \mathrm {F e} \left(\mathrm {C N}\right) _ {6} \right] ^ {3 -} + \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \leftrightarrow \left[ \mathrm {F e} \left(\mathrm {C N}\right) _ {6} \right] ^ {4 -} \quad E ^ {\circ} = 0. 3 6 \mathrm {V} \tag {63}
$$

Anode:

$$
2 \mathrm {H} _ {2} \mathrm {O} + 2 \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \leftrightarrow 2 \mathrm {O H} ^ {-} + \mathrm {H} _ {2} \quad E ^ {\circ} = - 0. 8 3 \mathrm {V} \tag {64}
$$

Overall:

$$
2 \left[ \mathrm {F e} (\mathrm {C N}) _ {6} \right] ^ {3 -} + 2 \mathrm {O H} ^ {-} + \mathrm {H} _ {2} \leftrightarrow 2 \left[ \mathrm {F e} (\mathrm {C N}) _ {6} \right] ^ {4 -} + 2 \mathrm {H} _ {2} \mathrm {O}
$$

$$
E ^ {\circ} = 1. 1 9 \mathrm {V} \tag {65}
$$

Nafion membranes with  $\mathrm{K}^+$  channels were chosen as the separator in order to transport the  $\mathrm{K}^+$  and prevent the crossover of liquid redox molecules. During battery charging,  $\mathrm{H}_2\mathrm{O}$  is reduced to  $\mathrm{H}_2$  gas by the  $\mathrm{Pt / C}$  catalyst and  $[\mathrm{Fe(CN)}_6]^{4 - }$  is oxidized to  $[\mathrm{Fe(CN)}_6]^{3 - }$  in the liquid state. Meanwhile, in order

to balance the cell charge,  $\mathrm{K}^+$  ions are transported through the Nafion membrane from cathode to anode; the reverse holds true for discharging. During electrochemical testing, the aqueous  $\mathrm{Fe - H_2}$  battery delivers a high discharge voltage plateau of 1.29 V at a current of  $10\mathrm{mA}$  (Figure 93b). The discharge voltage is maintained at a high potential of  $1.1\mathrm{V}$  even at a current as high as  $60\mathrm{mA}$ . The CE of the battery under each current is nearly  $100\%$ , which demonstrates excellent charge conversion performance (Figure 93c). The capacity retentions are recorded to be  $79\%$ ,  $70\%$ ,  $64\%$ ,  $61\%$ , and  $57\%$  under currents of 20, 30, 40, 50, and  $60\mathrm{mA}$ , respectively, as compared to that at  $10\mathrm{mA}$ . As a result, the battery delivers high EE of  $93\%$  at a low current of  $10\mathrm{mA}$  and over  $73\%$  even at a high current of  $60\mathrm{mA}$ . Furthermore, long-term cycling performance of the aqueous  $\mathrm{Fe - H_2}$  battery is measured at a charge/discharge current of  $20\mathrm{mA}$  with a charge capacity of  $0.3\mathrm{mAh}$ , resulting in excellent cycling stability with no capacity decay over 20000 cycles (Figure 93d).

9.2.7. Other HGBs. The halides of  $\mathrm{Cl}$ ,  $\mathrm{Br}$ , and I generally exhibit high solubility and suitable potentials when acting as aqueous cathodes.[722,756,757] Previously, the electrolysis of hydrogen chloride for storing  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas and chlorine has been proposed as a promising method of energy storage for the electric utility industries.[756] In this regard, a new  $\mathrm{Cl}_{2}-\mathrm{H}_{2}$  energy storage system based on a  $\mathrm{Cl}_{2} / \mathrm{Cl}^{-}$ redox couple cathode and a high-efficiency  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas anode has been reported.[756] Such a battery offers cost-effective manufacturing with improved conversion efficiency owing to its low-cost cathode.[758] Harnessing the superior property of  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas, a  $\mathrm{Br}_{2}-\mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery has also been investigated by NASA as a power source for space related applications.[759] This battery system exhibits high electric-to-electric efficiency due to rapid reaction kinetics of both the Br and  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas electrodes.[757,760,761] The  $\mathrm{Br}_{2}-\mathrm{H}_{2}$  battery system also provides a competitive advantage of low weight of

![](images/0c03c8d289551066b41219881c8f1fbc47773f04efef9c731ff50d01b0703bc3.jpg)  
a

![](images/e08b03c6880e5d2baa662483c85bcf7348c615c1d9c10f2baf7782a03702b2e8.jpg)  
b  
d

![](images/488ff67f6ecb45abedb4a262283539043539a847141a952f22edc5ec8b5ad124.jpg)

![](images/1c3c7f3a8a080002ed107ea85ae969d2824cc1943650881d8b9b4078c0b3476e.jpg)

![](images/b9ed439a8f23eace175f789a2a5d96532f2600c5aa7488a638833ef6ced0fd60.jpg)  
e  
Figure 95.  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  battery with the cathode  $\mathrm{I}^{-} / \mathrm{I}_2$  chemistry. (a) Schematic illustration of the  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  battery. (b) Charge/discharge profiles at a charge current of  $10\mathrm{C}$  ( $1\mathrm{C} = 0.25\mathrm{mA}\mathrm{cm}^{-2}$ ) with a capacity of  $0.9\mathrm{mAh}$  (DoC  $100\%$ ) and a discharge current of  $20\mathrm{C}$ . (c) Rate discharge capacities at a charge current of  $10\mathrm{C}$  with a capacity of  $0.5\mathrm{mAh}$  (DoC  $56\%$ ). (d) Cycling performance at a charge current of  $10\mathrm{C}$  with a capacity of  $0.1\mathrm{mAh}$  (DoC  $11\%$ ) and a discharge current of  $40\mathrm{C}$ . For panels b–d, electrolyte = 0.5 M KI with 0.5 M PBS,  $100\mu\mathrm{L}$ . (e) Rate performance at a charge voltage of  $0.8\mathrm{V}$  with a capacity of  $0.9\mathrm{mAh}$ . Electrolyte = 1 M KI with  $2\mathrm{M}$ $\mathrm{H}_3\mathrm{PO}_4$ ,  $75\mu\mathrm{L}$ . (f) Rate performance at a charge current of  $5\mathrm{mA}\mathrm{cm}^{-2}$  with a capacity of  $1.2\mathrm{mAh}$ . Electrolyte = 1.2 M KI with  $1.4\mathrm{M}$ $\mathrm{KHCO}_3$  and  $\mathrm{K}_2\mathrm{CO}_3$ ,  $75\mu\mathrm{L}$ . Reproduced with permission from ref 771. Copyright 2021 Wiley-VCH.

![](images/95b0820b7ad96a8802c7093a323e01d889df13c9563ba4bd2b298dca078e8573.jpg)  
f

electrodes, thereby reducing the proportion of the whole battery assembly in the space-based power sources. Therefore, this novel HGB system has massive prospects in further exploration and exploitation in LSES applications.

In relation to the  $\mathrm{Br}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  batteries, numerous additional studies have been dedicated to investigating their cyclic reversibility behavior for GSES. [762] Following their introduction, these  $\mathrm{Br}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  batteries have been extensively studied within the domain of RFBs due to their rapid response time and high EE. [510,762] However, the  $\mathrm{Br}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  RFBs use the flow of hydrogen gas as anode and  $\mathrm{HBr} / \mathrm{Br}_2$  mixed solution as liquid redox cathode. [510,762] The working principle of the  $\mathrm{Br}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  RFB is shown in Figure 94a along with its typical cell structure. During

charging, HBr entering the cathode is oxidized into  $\mathrm{Br}_2$ , and conversely, the  $\mathrm{Br}_2$  transforms into HBr during discharging. The  $\mathrm{Br}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  RFB operates principally based on the following redox reactions:

Cathode:

$$
\mathrm {B r} _ {2} + 2 \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \leftrightarrow 2 \mathrm {B r} ^ {-} \quad E ^ {\circ} = 1. 0 9 \mathrm {V} \tag {66}
$$

Anode:

$$
2 \mathrm {H} ^ {+} + 2 \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \leftrightarrow \mathrm {H} _ {2} \quad E ^ {\circ} = 0 \mathrm {V} \tag {67}
$$

Overall:

$$
\mathrm {B r} _ {2} + \mathrm {H} _ {2} \leftrightarrow 2 \mathrm {B r} ^ {-} + 2 \mathrm {H} ^ {+} \quad E ^ {\circ} = 1. 0 9 \mathrm {V} \tag {68}
$$

To understand the rate capability of the aforementioned  $\mathrm{Br}_2-$ $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  RFB, its electrochemical performance at various discharge current densities, exhibiting obvious discharge plateau of  $\sim 0.75$  V at  $0.5\mathrm{C},$  is illustrated in Figure 94b. The change of solution color can further demonstrate the battery reaction states of charge and discharge (Figure 94b). Nonetheless, the  $\mathrm{Br}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  RFB shows a low operating voltage of  $\sim 0.75\mathrm{V},$  hence sparing plenty of room for further enhancement of its energy density. In contrast to the acidic medium, the standard electrode potential of the  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas anode shows a lower potential in alkaline electrolyte. Based on this principle, the  $\mathrm{Br}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  cell system has also been explored in hybrid electrolytes with alkaline electrolyte interfacing with the anode and neutral or acidic electrolyte interfacing with the cathode.[722] In this regard, the alkaline  $\mathrm{Br}_2-$ $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  cells deliver higher energy densities than their corresponding acidic systems. However, the  $\mathrm{Br}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  cells in the flow battery architectures and hybrid systems often use complex devices and Nafion membrane, which hinders their qualification to meet the demands of sustainable LSES. Having mentioned that, it is clear that HGBs based on the superior liquid cathode still need to overcome numerous difficulties including high cost, manufacturing intricacy, and optimization of their operational chemistries.[763-765]

Based on the highly efficient HER/HOR activity of the  $\mathrm{H}_2$  gas and electrochemical hydrogenation/dehydrogenation of hydrogen storage molecules such as benzoquinone (BQ), a new quinone- $\mathrm{H}_2$  battery system has been studied.[720] The structural schematic of the quinone- $\mathrm{H}_2$  battery is shown in Figure 94c. It can be seen that the Nafion membrane is used in the quinone- $\mathrm{H}_2$  battery as the separator for allowing the passage of  $\mathrm{H}^+$  only. During charging, the hydroquinone  $\mathrm{QH}_2$  releases  $\mathrm{H}^+$  to form BQ (dehydrogenation) on the cathode surface while the anode generates  $\mathrm{H}_2$  gas. However, the reactions are reversed during discharging. The electrode reactions are shown as follows:

Cathode:

$$
\mathrm {Q H} _ {2} \leftrightarrow \mathrm {B Q} + 2 \mathrm {H} ^ {+} + 2 \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \tag {69}
$$

Anode:

$$
2 \mathrm {H} ^ {+} + 2 \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \leftrightarrow \mathrm {H} _ {2} \tag {70}
$$

Overall:

$$
\mathrm {Q H} _ {2} \leftrightarrow \mathrm {B Q} + \mathrm {H} _ {2} \tag {71}
$$

Upon electrochemical testing, the quinone-  $\mathrm{H}_2$  battery demonstrates excellent cycling stability at  $10\mathrm{mAcm}^{-2}$  along with capacity retention of  $\sim 92\%$  after 200 cycles, as demonstrated in Figure 94d.

In addition to Cl and Br, the  $\mathrm{I}_3^-$  /  $\mathrm{I}^-$  redox couple has also been used as the liquid-type cathode due to its low cost and high solubility  $(>8\mathrm{M})$  766,767 However, an expensive cation exchange membrane (i.e., Nafion) is often required to hinder the crossover of  $\mathrm{I}_3^-$ . Thereafter, a strategy was explored by encapsulating iodine in a microporous carbon host to avoid the formation of liquid  $\mathrm{I}_3^-$  768-770 Chen and co-workers designed an  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  battery that exploits liquid-solid conversion reactions of the  $\mathrm{I}^{-} / \mathrm{I}_2$  redox couple at the cathode and the electrocatalytic reactions of HER/HOR at the anode.771 The schematic of the proposed aqueous  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  battery is shown in Figure 95a. During the charge process,  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  is generated from the solution on the anode and  $\mathrm{I}_2$  is formed from the solution on the cathode. During the discharge process,  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  is oxidized to the solution on anode and  $\mathrm{I}_2$  is reduced back to  $\mathrm{I}^-$  on cathode. The

proposed aqueous  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  battery can thus be constructed based on the following redox reactions:

Cathode:

$$
I _ {2} + 2 e ^ {-} \leftrightarrow 2 I ^ {-} \quad E ^ {\circ} = 0. 5 4 \mathrm {V} \tag {72}
$$

Anode:

$$
2 \mathrm {H} _ {2} \mathrm {O} + 2 \mathrm {e} ^ {-} \leftrightarrow 2 \mathrm {O H} ^ {-} + \mathrm {H} _ {2} \quad E ^ {\circ} = - 0. 8 3 \mathrm {V} \tag {73}
$$

Overall:

$$
\mathrm {I} _ {2} + 2 \mathrm {O H} ^ {-} + \mathrm {H} _ {2} \leftrightarrow 2 \mathrm {I} ^ {-} + 2 \mathrm {H} _ {2} \mathrm {O} \quad E ^ {\circ} = 1. 3 7 \mathrm {V} \tag {74}
$$

The theoretical capacity at the corresponding depth of charge (DoC) of  $100\%$  in the  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  batteries is defined by considering that all  $\mathrm{I}^-$  in solution are fully converted to  $\mathrm{I}_2$ . Figure 95b shows the charge/discharge profiles of the  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  battery with a DoC of  $100\%$  by charging to  $1.3\mathrm{V}$ . It shows a pair of pronounced charge/discharge voltage plateaus of  $1\mathrm{V} / 0.84\mathrm{V}$  at a charge capacity of  $\sim 0.9\mathrm{mAh}$ .

As shown in Figure 95c, even at a high rate of  $100\mathrm{C}$ , the battery still delivers stable capacity retention with high CE (an average of  $97.5\%$ ), indicating the excellent electrochemical reversibility and high rate capability at large current densities. Further, the long-term cycling measurements show high reversibility of the battery (Figure 95d) as the discharge capacity has negligible change after 60000 cycles (DoC  $11\%$ ). The high CE of over  $97\%$  for each cycle indicates the high quantitative utilization of the electrical charge. To extend the application and demonstrate the versatility of the  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  battery, the electrochemical performance of the aqueous  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  batteries in acidic and alkaline electrolytes were also tested. Compared to the  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  batteries in the neutral electrolyte with a discharge voltage of  $\sim 0.84\mathrm{V}$ , the batteries in the acidic electrolyte have a lower discharge plateau of  $\sim 0.47\mathrm{V}$  (Figure 95e). Nevertheless, the VE and EEs showed only a slight decline of  $10\%$ , when the current density increased from 5 to  $10\mathrm{mA cm}^{-2}$  (Figure 95e), demonstrating the fast kinetics of the acidic  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  battery. Compared to the neutral and acidic  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  batteries, the alkaline  $\mathrm{I}_2 - \mathrm{H}_2$  batteries show a high discharge plateau of  $\sim 0.91\mathrm{V}$  at a discharge current of  $5\mathrm{mA cm}^{-2}$  with a charge capacity of 1.2 mAh (Figure 95f). The CE of over  $95\%$  remained nearly unchanged and the VE only decreased from  $71\%$  to  $60\%$  as the discharge current increased from 5 to  $15\mathrm{mA cm}^{-2}$ .

# 9.3. Summary and Future Perspectives for HGBs

$\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas is regarded as a form of green energy for future sustainable communities.[27] Although it is flammable over a wide range of concentrations from  $4\%$  to  $74.2\%$  by volume, it is very safe in the surroundings of pure  $\mathrm{H}_{2}$  gas, which is exactly the case in HGBs.[772] Therefore, it is highly believed that there is no safety issue in the development of HGBs for LSES if proper precautionary measures are complied with. In this section, we have discussed recent progress on the understanding and development of HGBs by integrating low-cost bifunctional catalysts with various cathode materials. The fabricated HGBs showed high capacities, fast-charging rates, and long cyclic stabilities under rational designs. However, the challenges of HGBs from academia to industry mainly include high cost, high self-discharge, low energy density, and poor battery manufacturing.

First, the preparation of high cost electrocatalysts and efficient hydrogen electrodes is still one of the biggest issues of the HGBs

![](images/e55af979799993d5c71082319f849d3efa8f915eb28aa1fbde56e09825c43e77.jpg)  
a

![](images/374dec5ca4a3e5bf668c1a0495920daf7f3fe7a3b49ac4eaf618a4a1566fd008.jpg)  
b  
Figure 96. Summary of (a) maturity and (b) key performance parameter comparisons for various BESSs.

for their development from academia to industry. $^{56}$  According to previous HGBs, the working mode and performance requirements of GSES are similar to those of aerospace energy storage except for the high-cost characteristics. $^{708}$  It is essential to continually explore novel, low-cost, and highly electroactive bifunctional catalysts for substantial improvement of the overall

performance of HGBs. Second, the self-discharge performance is a crucial factor to control the reaction kinetics at the interface of the electrode and electrolyte. $^{709,754}$  In terms of HGBs for GSES, the cathode materials can slowly react with hydrogen gas and water molecules to cause the decay of capacity. To improve the self-discharge performance of HGBs, future work could be

conducted on fabricating stable cathode materials, reinforcing the electrolyte optimization, and introducing advanced gas management of the whole battery system. Third, it is important to develop advanced cathode materials with high specific capacity and voltage to accomplish the advantages of HGBs with high energy densities. In addition, the expansion of the electrochemical windows of electrolyte can also improve the energy densities of HGBs. Currently, the typical choices of electrolytes are often single acidic, neutral, or alkaline aqueous solutions, which are limited by the potentials of HER and OER. As an alternative strategy, the decoupling of alkaline electrolyte in the anode and acidic electrolyte in the cathode is viable to widen the electrochemical window of the aqueous HGBs.[240] In addition, the introduction of WIS electrolyte is promising for addressing the low voltage issue in the aqueous systems. The voltage of the aqueous HGBs can possibly be enlarged up to  $4\mathrm{V}$  with highly concentrated electrolytes of different compositions by tuning the electrolyte solvation structures.[773] Moreover, the cell voltages can be enhanced by utilizing innovative organic, IL, and solid-state electrolytes for reducing or removing water out of the electrolytes.[774] Furthermore, the efficient manufacturing of HGBs is highly important to the large-scale production of HGBs for GSES application. To take full advantages of the HGBs, it requires in-depth understanding of the application scenarios with different cell chemistries (including  $\mathrm{Ni - H_2}$ ,  $\mathrm{Mn - H_2}$ , and  $\mathrm{PBA - H_2}$  batteries) and form factors (prismatic, cylindrical, and pouch cells).[56,709,753] Therefore, the challenges in academic and industrial metrics need to be coordinated, and much research and development needs to be conducted accordingly.

# 10. SUMMARY AND PERSPECTIVE

# 10.1. Comparison and Potential of Battery Energy Storage Technologies

According to the maturity of research and development, the battery technologies can be generally divided into three different categories as shown in Figure 96a: (1) mature technologies, including LIBs, LABs, Ni-MH batteries, Pb-C batteries, MSBs, VRFBs, etc.; (2) technologies under development, including SIBs, ZIBs, ZBBs, ICBs,  $\mathrm{Ni - H_2}$  batteries, Zn-air batteries, solid-state LIBs, etc.; (3) emerging technologies, including ALIBs, organic RFBs, nonaqueous RFBs, semisolid RFBs, Ni-Zn batteries, PIBs, MgIBs, AIBs, Mg-air batteries, Al-air batteries, HGBs, etc.

Figure 96b shows the summary and comparison of some key performance parameters of battery technologies. It is evident that LIBs dominate the markets of portable electronics and power battery systems. Despite limited Li resources and flammability of organic electrolytes, the declining cost and perpetual performance improvements in response to stringent GSES have rendered Li-ion systems highly sought-after in stationary energy storage applications. Solid-state LIBs with high safety, SIBs with abundant resources, and ZIBs with high safety and low cost are still under development at the current technology levels.[79] Other MIBs (including  $\mathrm{K}^+$ ,  $\mathrm{Mg}^{2+}$ , and  $\mathrm{Al}^{3+}$ ), despite their abundant element reserves and better safety features, do not meet comprehensive performance requirements of GSES at the current technology levels.[79] This immediately calls for significant momentum toward the exploration of novel electrode materials as well as stable electrolytes for their GSES applications. In this regard, the replacement of flammable organic electrolytes with aqueous electrolytes is becoming the cornerstone of modern research on developing next generation

LIBs in emerging technology. However, notwithstanding massive potential for catering to GSES needs, this advancement poses its own corresponding challenges, including short life and high costs.

LABs are a relatively more mature and cost-effective technology when compared with other battery chemistries, with relatively short cycle life and sluggish charging rendering them impractical for GSES.[291] However, modernistic design integrating LABs with  $\mathrm{Pb - C}$  asymmetric capacitors has enabled it to operate with unprecedented efficiency for longer periods of time for applications requiring HRPSoC.[299] Although still offering insufficient service life for BESSs, the advantages of low cost and enhanced safety have attracted widespread utility of LAB systems in several medium- and small-scale energy storage applications.

The MSBs under development suffer from safety risks at high operating temperatures and poor heat management.[775] In relation to low- and medium-temperature Na-S batteries, the deteriorating electrochemical performance in terms of short cycle life and high self-discharge upon subsequent cycling also limits their extensive scope of application.[341] In contrast to Na-S batteries, LMBs offer advantages including high capacity, low manufacturing cost, and long cycle life, thereby paving their way to broad application prospects in GSES.[389] It is imperative to mention that the futuristic research on LMBs is expected to focus on new electrode materials, thermal management (at lower operating temperature), and avoidance of high temperature corrosion and leakage.[389] Furthermore, ZEBRA batteries are much safer than Na-S batteries due to the presence of metal halides, which are generally less corrosive than sodium polysulfide,[376,377] not to mention that the cycle stability of ZEBRA batteries still has substantial room for improvement for GSES applications.

Concerning the ABs, besides the rampant use of Ni-MH batteries in stationary applications, the issues of capacity fade upon repetitive cycling and high self-discharge persist and therefore still require substantial improvements.[436] In addition, Ni-Zn batteries show reasonable potential for future GSES applications owing to the crustal abundance of their constituent elements.[440] However, long-term stability and negligible formation of Zn dendrites in Ni-Zn batteries are yet to be realized.

VRFBs have earned the reputation of mature technologies for GSES, thanks to their inherent safety and long cycle life. The VRFB chemistries also come with imperfections in terms of low energy density and scarcity of vanadium element, which increase their total manufacturing cost.[508] In this regard, the nonaqueous electrolytes yield high voltage and broaden the choice of redox species at the expense of compromised safety, redox concentration, and power densities. Furthermore, inexpensive and sustainable organic redox materials have emerged as wholesome alternatives to the present metal-based redox species.[536] It is believed that redox potential and solubility can be tailored by introducing specific side groups on the organic molecular structures. Although the long-term stability of organic redox species has not yet been verified, the organic RFBs with advanced porous membranes are speculated to be one of the most promising, inexpensive, and highly efficient candidates as next-generation RFBs for GSES. In addition, semisolid RFBs and SFBs, although still in their infancy, are promising for exhibiting unique advantages for future GSES.[541,555]

As one of the typical aqueous MABs (Zn, Fe, Al, and Mg), the Zn-air battery system has the ability to yield a theoretical energy

![](images/9087dd0c84c38107a1655362c8f662795b430dde3c103bfbdeb04297facf5ce9.jpg)  
Figure 97. Development model of BESS from fundamental research to various applications (note: O&M = operations and maintenance; E&S = environment and safety; CD = current density; DoD = depth of discharge; BMS = battery management systems; PCS = power conversion system; BOP = balance of plant; C&C = construction and commissioning; UPS = unattended power source).

density of  $1353\mathrm{Whkg}^{-1}$  (excluding oxygen) and extremely low fabrication cost.[42,559] However, the practically attainable energy density of a Zn-air battery is usually between 350 and 500 Wh  $\mathrm{kg}^{-1}$ , not to mention that the commercialized Zn-air devices have inadequate rate capability, cycle life, and EE (less than  $60\%$ ).[595] The OER/ORR redox kinetics of the air catalysts along with the cathode architectures play a decisive role in augmenting Zn-air battery performance. Similarly, the metallic anode needs to be exclusively engineered to suppress its corrosion and nonuniform dissolution and deposition during reversible cycling. However, the studies on curbing the electrolytic decomposition in nonaqueous MABs (metals such as Li, Na, and K) are still in their infancy.

In addition, the state-of-the-art HGBs, such as advanced  $\mathrm{Ni}-\mathrm{H}_2$  and  $\mathrm{Mn}-\mathrm{H}_2$  cells, offer superior electrochemical performance among previously reported BESSs.[56,709] In this regard, the highly efficient and fast HER/HOR reactions occurring at electrodes are highly promising toward commercially viable, safe, low cost, and long-life hydrogen-based BESSs. Recently, advanced  $\mathrm{Ni}-\mathrm{H}_2$  batteries have been commercialized by the

EnerVenue startup, and it announced an agreement with Pine Gate Renewables to supply 2.4 GWh advanced  $\mathrm{Ni - H_2}$  battery systems for GSES. As for other HGBs, there is urgent need for further performance improvements through developing highly efficient electrodes, cell management systems, and highly active and earth-abundant HER/HOR catalysts.

# 10.2. Future Development of Grid Scale Battery Systems

Currently, there is no ideal battery technology that can meet all the comprehensive requirements of GSES. This calls for the immediate action, carrying out breakthrough studies toward solving key performance issues of batteries and rendering their novel designs viable for GSES. Despite concerns of diminishing lithium reserves and poor safety, LIBs have been one of the most successful technologies in the history of the BESS field. Considering the abundant sodium reserves, SIBs have yet-to-be-harnessed potential to supplement or even replace LIBs in the field of GSES. When it comes to the safety and cost effectiveness of energy storage devices, the VRFB and HGB technologies have untapped potential for worldwide industrial

ization. In addition, other potential battery technologies with unsatisfying electrochemical performances cannot meet the stringent demands for large-scale commercialization and therefore need further improvements.

At present, there is utmost urgency to invest hefty capital in research and development to come up with cutting-edge battery technologies for catering to the stationary and mobile energy storage needs and ensuring long-term returns. In this regard, governments are playing a pivotal role in BESS research and demonstration projects by providing financial, material, and logistic support for establishing industrial facilities and ensuring streamlined energy practices. The increased proclivity toward VRE is speculated to be the key economic driving force in countries who seek to advance grid flexibility and maximize renewable resource feed-in. Last but not least, investment institutions and leading manufacturing enterprises are also expected to pour their efforts in developing better battery technologies for GSES.

# 10.3. Integrated Approaches for Grid Scale Battery Systems

A developmental model of BESS illustrating the basic elements of battery research and various applications is shown in Figure 97. Following the breakthroughs in fundamental energy storage research, there is need to further realize achievements in energy materials and novel BESS prototype designs, yielding suitable performance for specific applications. These applications include household photovoltaic energy, communication base stations, UPS, PV charging stations, microgrids, user side energy storage, and other small- and medium-scale uses, as well as large-scale applications such as integration of bulk renewables. In relation to these, the installation costs, estimated project lifetime, environment and security standards, duration, power rating, construction and commissioning, and operation and management are the paramount considerations. On the other hand, the corresponding evaluation parameters of battery and cell prototypes include capital cost, cycle life, material stability, intrinsic safety, capacity, voltage, current density, energy density, self-discharge, and operating temperature range. Upon developing potential performing battery prototypes or modules on the laboratory scale, equally important is establishing the corresponding industrialization and commercialization model from raw material supply to factory manufacturing. Additional key design aspects such as room for scaling-up through stacking and overall battery management systems (BMSs) are also crucial for improving the capacity, power, and reliability of battery technology. The battery rack for watt-to-kilowatt scaling can be trial-tested for practical small-scale energy storage applications. After passing the performance test, the battery rack, system PCS, BMS, and other auxiliary equipment can be assembled into a containerized BESS, which can then be utilized for medium-scale energy storage. Finally, upon performing satisfactorily for small- and medium-scale storage, the containerized BESS can be subjected to further scale-up through bulk-construction layout to achieve the technology shift toward large-scale industrial grid energy storage. In the past decade, some breakthrough battery technologies have attempted to experience the aforementioned small-scale to large-scale transformation; nonetheless most of them have been unable to meet the requirements of commercialization yet. The ongoing emergence of novel battery chemistries is also bringing many technical challenges. Therefore, BESS researchers are encouraged to focus on solving scientific bottlenecks, by designing practical batteries and transforming the lab-scale cells into commercially viable

technologies for ensuring the sustainable future of energy storage.

# Biographies

Zhengxin Zhu is a postdoctoral researcher in the Hefei National Research Center for Physical Sciences at the Microscale of the University of Science and Technology of China (USTC). He obtained his B.S. degree from China University of Geosciences (Wuhan) in 2017 and his Ph.D. degree in inorganic chemistry from USTC in 2022. He is currently working under the supervision of Prof. Wei Chen at USTC. His research interests focus on aqueous rechargeable hydrogen gas batteries for GSES.

Taoli Jiang is a Ph.D. candidate in the department of applied chemistry of the University of Science and Technology of China (USTC). He obtained his B.S. degree from Central South University of Forestry and Technology in 2017 and his M.S. degree from University of Science and Technology Beijing in 2020. He is currently under the supervision of

Prof. Wei Chen at USTC. His research focuses on hydrogen energy and advanced long-life batteries for GSES.

Mohsin Ali is a Ph.D. student in the Department of Applied Chemistry of the University of Science and Technology of China (USTC). He obtained his B.S. degree from Ghulam Ishaq Khan (GIK) Institute Pakistan in 2013 and his M.S. degree from Dalian University of Technology (DUT) in China in 2018. He is currently working under the supervision of Professor Wei Chen at USTC. His research focuses on novel metal batteries and electrocatalysis.

Yahan Meng is a M.S. candidate in the department of applied chemistry of the University of Science and Technology of China (USTC). She obtained her B.S. degree from Nanjing University of Science and Technology in 2020. She is currently under the supervision of Prof. Wei Chen at USTC. Her research focuses on hydrogen gas batteries.

Yang Jin is an Associate Professor in the school of electrical engineering of the Zhengzhou University. He obtained his B.S. degree from Zhengzhou University in 2012 and his Ph.D. degree from Xi'an Jiaotong University in 2017. His research interests involve battery energy storage, grid energy storage, and battery safety.

Yi Cui is a Professor in the Department of Materials Science and Engineering at Stanford University and SLAC National Accelerator Laboratory. He received his B.S. from the University of Science and Technology of China in 1998 and his Ph.D. from Harvard University in 2002. He was a Miller Postdoctoral Fellow at University of California, Berkeley, and joined Stanford as a faculty member in 2005. His current research is on nanomaterials for energy and environment. He has founded four companies to commercialize technologies from his lab: Amprius, 4C Air, EEnotech, and EnerVenue.

Wei Chen is a Professor in the department of applied chemistry of the University of Science and Technology of China (USTC) and the Hefei National Research Center for Physical Sciences at the Microscale. He obtained his B.S. degree in materials physics from University of Science and Technology Beijing in 2008 and his Ph.D. degree in materials science and engineering from King Abdullah University of Science and Technology (KAUST) in 2013. He then worked as a postdoctoral researcher at Stanford University under the supervision of Prof. Yi Cui in 2014 and joined EEnotech in 2018 as a scientist before joining in USTC in 2019. His research interests involve advanced materials and technologies for energy storage and catalysis.
